:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit with the legs extended in front of the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bend one leg and place its foot on top of the opposite thigh. The sole
of the foot must be upward, with the heel facing or touching the pelvis.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bend the other leg and place its foot on top of the other thigh.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The spine should be held straight, the neck, head and shoulders should
be relaxed and the body should be steady.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Contra-indications]{.class5829-0} [: Those who suffer from sciatica,
sacral infections or weak or injured knees should not perform this
asana. This asana should not be attempted until flexibility of the knees
has been developed.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Benefits]{.class5829-0} [: Padmasana allows the body to be held
completely steady for long periods of time. It holds the trunk and head
like a pillar with the legs as the firm foundation. As the body is
steadied the mind becomes calm. This steadiness and calmness is the
first step towards real meditation. Padmasana directs the flow of prana
from mooladhara chakra in the perineum, to sahasrara chakra in the head,
heightening the experience of meditation.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {#part0038.xhtml_page_207 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
This posture applies pressure to the lower spine which has a relaxing
effect on the nervous system. The breath becomes slow, muscular tension
is decreased and blood pressure is reduced.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The coccygeal and sacral nerves are toned as the normally large blood
flow to the legs is redirected towards the abdominal region. This
activity also stimulates the digestive process.
:::

::: class1545-1
![](image1544.jpg){.class1545-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Utthanpadasana (stretched leg pose)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit with both legs extended in front of the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bend the left knee and press the left heel firmly into the perineum or
the entrance to the vagina, the location point of mooladhara chakra. The
right leg remains outstretched.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Place both hands on the right knee.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Adjust the position so that it is comfortable.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bend forward just enough to be able to clasp the right big toe with both
hands.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold the position for a comfortable duration.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Return to the upright position with both hands resting on the right
knee.
:::

::: class1557-1
![](image1556.jpg){.class1557-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Bhadrasana (gracious pose)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {#part0038.xhtml_page_208 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in vajrasana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Separate the knees as far as possible, while keeping the toes in contact
with the floor.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Separate the feet just enough to allow the buttocks and perineum to rest
flat on the floor between the feet.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to separate the knees further but do not strain.
:::

::: {.class1564 lang="en-us"}
Place the hands on the knees, palms down, and make the back straight.
:::

[]{#part0039.xhtml}

::: {#part0039.xhtml_page_209 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[27](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5857)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Chakra Sadhana Course](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5857)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[M]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} onth by month we have given specific
practices for the awakening of each chakra, one after the other. These
practices must be adopted systematically. For the first month, you
should only perform the techniques for ajna chakra. Then in the second
month, add those for mooladhara. In the third month, add those for
swadhisthana. In the fourth month, do those practices for manipura and
selected practices for ajna, mooladhara and swadhisthana chakras. (By
this stage, due to the number of practices, it will be necessary to omit
some.) In this way, you should continue, adding the practices for each
chakra, until you reach bindu during the seventh month.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[The first month is concerned with awakening ajna chakra and not the
lowest one, mooladhara, which is treated in the second month. It may
seem more logical and consistent to start with mooladhara practices, but
it is a rule of kundalini yoga that there should be awakening of ajna
chakra first. Unless this is achieved, then the awakening of the lower
chakras may rock the stability of the practitioner; one may experience
physical, mental and emotional shocks which one cannot bear. The
awakening of ajna chakra brings a great degree of detachment, which
allows one to withstand the lower chakra awakenings without excessive
shock. One is able to observe chakra experiences with the attitude of a
witness. This is most essential in kundalini yoga.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {#part0039.xhtml_page_210 .class179 lang="en-us"}
[In the eighth month we have given some practices which influence the
chakras as a whole. These should also be done for one month.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Please note that some practices influence more than one chakra, but we
have only given each practice once as sadhana for the chakra it is most
likely to affect. Also, it should be noted that nothing can be gained by
randomly selecting one chakra sadhana program and just practising it for
a day or two and then commencing another practice. As each practice is a
stepping-stone for another practice, the techniques should be performed
systematically. In each chapter, practices are given to locate the
position of the]{.class-0} [chakra]{.class5827-1} [, and its
counterpart, the]{.class-0} [kshetram]{.class5827-1} [(which is located
in the front of the body). It is important that you can locate these
points exactly.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[The practices given for each chakra are the building blocks from which
the kriya yoga techniques are constructed. As such, you should perfect
them before proceeding to the kriyas. Ultimately, you will only need to
practise the kriyas, but prior to this you must devote at least one hour
a day to the chakra practices for the next eight months.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Kriya yoga
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
In [chapter 38](#part0050.xhtml) we have given a full description of the
twenty kundalini kriyas, which are widely known as kriya yoga. At this
stage, you can leave all the specific practices given in the previous
chapters for awakening the chakras individually, or if you wish you can
select a few to continue with.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[The kundalini kriyas can be learned and practised one after the other,
at the rate of one per week. That is, in the first week perfect
vipareeta karani mudra; in the second week add chakra anusandhana; then
add nada sanchalana in the third week, and so on. At the end of twenty
weeks you should be doing the entire series of twenty kriyas daily, with
the traditional number of rounds for each kriya, or with a reduced
number of rounds as indicated.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class202 lang="en-us"}
[Please note that the kundalini kriyas should only be practised under
the guidance of a qualified teacher.]{.class-0}
:::

[]{#part0040.xhtml}

::: {#part0040.xhtml_page_211 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[28](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5864)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Practices for Ajna Chakra](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5864)
:::

::: {#part0040.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5862 .class1589 lang="en-us"}
[MONTH 1](#part0048.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5918)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[D]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} irect concentration on ajna chakra is very
difficult and, for this reason, in tantra and yoga the mid-eyebrow
centre (which in fact is the kshetram of ajna) is used to awaken this
chakra. This point is called bhrumadhya ([bhru]{.class5827-0} means
eyebrow and [madhya]{.class5827-0} means centre), and it lies between
the two eyebrows in the place where Indian ladies put a red dot, and
pandits and brahmins put a mark of sandal paste. This eyebrow centre can
be stimulated and awakened by various techniques.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Firstly, there is an important shatkriya (cleansing technique)
called]{.class-0} [trataka]{.class5827-1} [, which will aid in the
awakening of ajna. It is a powerful technique which can be defined as
'fixed gazing at one point'. If practised regularly, it develops the
power of concentration and from this concentration, the direct awakening
of the latent faculties of ajna chakra is brought about.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Ajna can also be stimulated and awakened by concentration on the nadis
directly. The method for this is]{.class-0} [anuloma viloma
pranayama]{.class5827-1} [, mental or psychic nadi shodhana, also known
as 'the coming and going pranayama', and]{.class-0} [prana
shuddhi]{.class5827-1} [, 'the purifying breath'.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[You can also awaken ajna chakra by concentrating on the eyebrow centre,
performing such practices as]{.class-0} [shambhavi mudra]{.class5827-1}
[. Initially, when there is no sensation or awareness at this point,
some ointment or oil such as tiger balm can be]{.class-0}
[]{#part0040.xhtml_page_212 .class-0} [applied. This facilitates
concentration. With practise, the pressure of your concentration at this
area increases and the sensations are carried back to the pineal gland.
This brings about an awakening in the pineal gland in the form of
visions and internal experiences.]{.class-0}
:::

::: class1412-0
![](image1596.jpg){.class1412-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1598 lang="en-us"}
Ajna
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Ajna and mooladhara chakras are closely related, and the awakening of
one helps to awaken the other. Ideally, ajna should be awakened to some
extent before mooladhara, in order to allow an unaffected perception of
the energies manifested by mooladhara and the lower chakras. However,
the awakening of mooladhara will help to further awaken ajna. In fact,
the best way to bring about awakening of ajna is through the practices
of]{.class-0} [moola bandha]{.class5827-1} [and]{.class-0}
[ashwini]{.class5827-1} [mudra]{.class5827-1} [, which are specific for
mooladhara.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Preparatory practices
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Jala]{.class5827-0} and [sutra neti]{.class5827-0} can be practised for
a few months to purify the nasal area and the important nerve junction
behind it. This will help to sensitize ajna chakra and aid in its
awakening. Apart from having a profound effect on the nervous system,
neti removes dirt and mucus from the nasal passages, relieving colds and
sinusitis, disorders of the eyes, ears, nose and throat, as well as
inflammation of the tonsils, adenoids and mucous membranes. It removes
drowsiness and gives a general lightness and freshness in the head and
throughout the body. At the same time, it profoundly alters psychic
awareness, facilitating free flow of breath in both nostrils, so that
the meditative state can be attained. It should be practised every
morning before you commence your other sadhana. For complete details
refer to the Bihar School of Yoga publication [Asana Pranayama Mudra
Bandha]{.class5827-0} .
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice program
:::

::: {#part0040.xhtml_page_213 .class52 lang="en-us"}
The following sadhana (consisting of practices 1, 2 and 3) for ajna
chakra should be continued daily for one month. You may then proceed to
the sadhana given for awakening mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 1: Anuloma Viloma Pranayama with Prana Shuddhi (the coming and
going breath and the purifying breath)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in a comfortable meditative posture.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Make sure the spine is erect and the body is relaxed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The body must become absolutely still.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After some minutes, begin to develop awareness of the breath in the
nostrils.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you breathe in, your whole awareness should flow with the breath
from the tip of the nose, up to the eyebrow centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you breathe out, your whole awareness should flow with the breath
from the eyebrow centre to the tip of the nose.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of the triangular form of the breath between the nostrils
and the eyebrow centre. The base of the triangle is at the level of the
upper lip, its sides are the right and left nasal passages, and its apex
is within the eyebrow centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Firstly, feel the breath moving in and out of the left nostril, then the
right nostril. Then be aware of the breath as it flows in and out
through both nostrils together.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Once you are established in this breath awareness, begin to consciously
alternate the flow of the breath between the two nostrils in the same
way as nadi shodhana, except you practise it psychically or mentally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Consciously inhale through the left nostril to bhrumadhya and exhale
through the right, then inhale through the right to bhrumadhya, and
exhale through the left.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is one round of anuloma viloma or mental nadi shodhana. Complete 4
rounds.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now practise one round of prana shuddhi, which involves breathing in and
out through both nostrils together.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale and exhale through both nostrils simultaneously, visualizing the
passage of the breath forming an inverted V-shape.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue in this way: four alternate nostril breaths, then one breath
through both nostrils.
:::

::: {#part0040.xhtml_page_214 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
In the beginning, the rounds can be counted as follows:
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
1 -- inhale left nostril, exhale right nostril; inhale right nostril,
exhale left nostril,
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
2 -- repeat, 3 -- repeat, 4 -- repeat,
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
5 -- inhale both nostrils, exhale both nostrils, and so on.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After some practise, the rounds can be counted from 100 back to zero as
follows:
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
100 -- inhale left nostril, exhale right nostril; inhale right nostril,
exhale left nostril,
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
99 -- repeat, 98 -- repeat, 97 -- repeat,
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
96 -- inhale both nostrils, exhale both nostrils, and so on.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Accuracy in the counting is absolutely
necessary, and if an error is made, the practice must recommence from
100. It is very important to keep count of the breaths, because without
keeping count, anuloma viloma is altogether too powerful for many
aspirants, swallowing up their awareness in the unconscious
sphere.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The aim of the practice is to stimulate ajna chakra on the subconscious,
psychic level, and for this, awareness must be maintained.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If you sink into the unconscious sphere, you will only be aware of the
vast store of impressions in the unconscious mind, and will completely
lose awareness of the practice. This awareness is essential for the
development of mind control and also for the awakening of ajna chakra to
conscious accessibility.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This practice can also be very well integrated into yoga nidra. (See
[chapter 35](#part0047.xhtml) .)
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 2: Trataka (concentrated gazing)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in a comfortable meditative asana, in a dark room in which there is
no draught or breeze.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Place a lighted candle at eye level, directly in front of the eyebrow
centre, at arm's length.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Make sure that the wick is perfectly straight and that the flame is
motionless.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Straighten the spine, close the eyes and relax the body.
:::

::: class1640-0
![](image1639.jpg){#page_215 .class1640-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1642 lang="en-us"}
Be aware of the physical body only. Let it become as still as a statue.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
From this time on you should try to keep the body absolutely motionless
throughout the whole practice. When you are prepared, open your eyes and
gaze steadily at the tip of the wick. With practise you should be able
to gaze steadily at the flame without blinking or moving the eyeballs.
Two to three minutes is sufficient.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The whole of your consciousness must become centred in the flame, to the
extent that awareness of the rest of the body and the room is lost. The
gaze should be absolutely fixed at the tip of the wick. When the eyes
become tired or if they begin to water, close them and relax.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not move the body, but be aware of the after-image of the flame in
front of the closed eyes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Everyone has looked into the sun or a bright light, and on closing the
eyes for a few minutes, has seen the clear impression of that light on
the retina of the eye. Likewise, the after-image of the candle flame
will be clearly visible.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
You should practise trataka on this image, holding it directly in front
or a little above the eyebrow centre. Keep the eyes closed. If the image
moves up or down, or from side to side, observe it and try to stabilize
it, without straining.
:::

::: {#part0040.xhtml_page_216 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you are sure the image has appeared and faded for the last time,
then open the eyes and continue to concentrate on the external candle
flame.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After the last round, gaze into the emptiness for a few seconds then
practise palming.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Time of practice]{.class5829-0} [: The best times to practise trataka
are the dark hours of the very early morning or late at night. At these
times, the atmosphere becomes very still and quiet, not only the
physical atmosphere, but also the mental and psychic atmospheres. In
this stillness, success in trataka is readily attained.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Duration]{.class5829-0} [: Trataka can be practised as time permits,
but five to fifteen minutes is the usual period in the beginning,
building up to thirty minutes gradually over a period of time. Two to
three minutes per round is sufficient to spend gazing at the
flame.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Contra-indications]{.class5829-0} [: Trataka on a flame is not
recommended for myopia, astigmatism, cataract or glaucoma.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Benefits]{.class5829-0} [: Trataka has many physical, mental and
spiritual benefits. Physically, it corrects eye weaknesses and defects
such as nearsightedness. Mentally, it increases nervous stability,
removes insomnia and relaxes the anxious mind. When the eyes are fixed
and unmoving, the mind becomes steady and calm. It helps to develop good
concentration and strong willpower. Spiritually it awakens ajna
chakra.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Variations]{.class5829-0} [: Trataka can be practised on a small dot,
the full moon, the rising sun, a shadow, a crystal ball, the nose tip,
an image in water, a yantra, darkness, a shivalingam and many other
things.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Those who have a personal deity can practise trataka on his or her form
and those who have a guru can practise on his or her photograph. Trataka
can also be practised on one's own image in the mirror, or the eyes of
another person. These should, however, only be done under the guidance
of a guru, as there are certain risks involved.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Avoid practising trataka on the sun as the delicate membranes of the
eyes may be damaged.
:::

::: {#part0040.xhtml_page_217 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
There are two divisions of trataka, [bahiranga]{.class5827-0} (outer)
and [antaranga]{.class5827-0} (inner). The methods mentioned so far are
all part of bahiranga trataka. Inner trataka (antaranga) is internal
visualization, perhaps of a chakra, a yantra or your personal deity. The
eyes remain closed throughout. One of the best inner objects for
concentration is a tiny star or point of light.
:::

::: class1661-0
![](image1660.jpg){.class1661-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 3: Shambhavi Mudra (eyebrow centre gazing) with Om
chanting]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 1: External awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in any meditative pose with the back straight and hands on the
knees.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Look forward at a fixed point, then look upward as high as possible
without moving the head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Focus the eyes and concentrate on the eyebrow centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to suspend the thought processes and meditate on ajna.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat Om, Om, Om with awareness of the sound vibrations at the eyebrow
centre into which you are gazing. Each Om should be produced in a soft
clear voice, with awareness of every vibration of the mantra in the
eyebrow centre.
:::

::: {#part0040.xhtml_page_218 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Each mantra should be one or two seconds in duration, and immediately
followed by the next.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise for three to five minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 2: Internal awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now the eyes are closed, but the inner gaze remains in the eyebrow
centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Begin to chant the mantra more slowly, with full awareness of the sound
vibration in the eyebrow centre. Imagine that the sound is being emitted
from within the eyebrow centre itself. Gradually and effortlessly
increase the duration of each Om, making it long and continuous.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The sound should be steady and of an even key, ending on completion of
the breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then refill the lungs completely by breathing through the nose, but do
not alter the position of the body or head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Begin the next Om, maintaining awareness of the sound emerging from the
eyebrow centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise for five minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 3: Awareness of sound vibration]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue to chant the mantra Om, but become aware of the sound
reverberating throughout the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to be aware of the sound only, listening to its vibration emanating
from the eyebrow centre and permeating the whole body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not be self-conscious, but allow the sound to manifest itself fully,
maintaining awareness of the vibration of the sound only.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise for five minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Gradually the duration of the practice can be lengthened.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Finish off the practice with palming.
:::

::: {.class1686 lang="en-us"}
[Precautions]{.class5829-0} [: Do not strain the eye muscles; when they
become tired or slightly strained, release shambhavi mudra and relax the
eyes.]{.class-4}
:::

[]{#part0041.xhtml}

::: {#part0041.xhtml_page_219 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[29](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5859)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Practices for\
Mooladhara Chakra](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5859)
:::

::: {#part0041.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5993 .class1589 lang="en-us"}
[MONTH 2](#part0048.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5966)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[T]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} he process of awakening mooladhara chakra is
not very difficult. It can be achieved by thousands of different
methods, but the easiest of all is the concentration on the tip of the
nose. This is because the part of the sensory cortex which represents
mooladhara chakra is connected with the nose. At the same time,
mooladhara chakra belongs to the earth element, which is directly
related to the sense of smell. Therefore, we shall include [nasikagra
drishti]{.class5827-0} , the practice of nose tip gazing, in this
section, as well as moola bandha, which directly stimulates mooladhara
chakra. Remember that mooladhara chakra does not have a kshetram.
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice program
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
This sadhana (practices 1, 2 and 3) for mooladhara chakra should be done
for a period of one month. You should also continue the practices for
awakening ajna chakra.
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Difference between moola bandha, vajroli/sahajoli mudra and ashwini
mudra
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Often there is confusion between the three practices of moola bandha
(used for awakening mooladhara chakra) and vajroli/sahajoli mudra and
ashwini mudra (both used for awakening swadhisthana chakra). The
following diagrams for both male and female locations will help to
clarify the difference in the points of contraction.
:::

::: class1412-0
![](image1702.jpg){.class1412-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1414 lang="en-us"}
Mooladhara
:::

::: class1707-0
![](image1706.jpg){#page_220 .class1707-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1709 lang="en-us"}
Diagram 1: for the female
:::

::: {.class1711 lang="en-us"}
Key to location of contraction points: (1) Sahajoli mudra (clitoris,
vaginal walls and urethra); (2) Moola bandha (cervix and vaginal
muscles); (3) Ashwini mudra (anal muscles/sphincters).
:::

::: class1715-1
![](image1714.jpg){.class1715-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1709 lang="en-us"}
Diagram 2: for the male
:::

::: {.class1711 lang="en-us"}
Key to location of contraction points: (1) Vajroli mudra (penis);(2)
Moola bandha (between anus and scrotum; the perineal body); (3) Ashwini
mudra (anal muscles/sphincters).
:::

::: {#part0041.xhtml_page_221 .class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 1: Mooladhara chakra location]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[For men]{.class5829-0} [: Sit in siddhasana or any asana in which the
heel is pressed into the perineum.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes, relax completely and become aware of the whole physical
body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Move the awareness to the point of contact between the heel and
perineum, midway between the testes and the anus. Become intensely aware
of the distinct pressure exerted on the perineal body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Centre yourself at the pressure point.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now become aware of the breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel or imagine that you are breathing in and out of this pressure
point.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel the breath moving through the perineal body, becoming finer and
finer, and finer, so that it pierces the point where mooladhara chakra
is located.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
You will feel it as a psychophysical contraction.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Say mentally, 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Maintain awareness of the perineal body and the breath for up to five
minutes.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[For women]{.class5829-0} [: Sit in siddha yoni asana or a suitable
alternative.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Relax the body completely and close the eyes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Move the awareness to the lower part of the body and focus the attention
on the contact point between the heel and the opening of the vagina.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become intensely aware of the slight but distinct pressure.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Centre yourself at the pressure point.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now become aware of the natural breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel or imagine that you are breathing in and out of the pressure point.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue for 10 deep breaths.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now bring your awareness inside the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
From the point of external pressure, move your awareness in towards the
base of the spine.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Follow the natural formation of the vagina, moving up at a slight angle
and back towards the spine until you come to the opening of the womb.
:::

::: {#part0041.xhtml_page_222 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
You are at the opening of the womb, about two or three centimetres
inside the body, just below the base of the spine.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Focus your awareness at this point and begin to breathe in and out from
the cervix to the point of outer pressure.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breathe in and bring your awareness to the opening of the womb.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breathe out and move again to the outer pressure point, the opening of
the vagina.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Somewhere in this area you will find your point for mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel this point clearly and distinctly and mentally repeat, 'mooladhara,
mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Maintain unbroken awareness of this point for up to five minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Alternative practice: Locating mooladhara chakra by touch]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[For men]{.class5829-0} [: Sit in a comfortable position and press one
finger onto the perineum, midway between the anus and scrotum, then
contract the muscles there. The contraction will be felt. When you can
contract those muscles without movement of the anus or penis, the
perineal body has been successfully isolated.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[For women:]{.class5829-0} [Assume a comfortable sitting or lying
position and gently insert one finger into the vagina as far as it will
go. Then contract the vaginal muscles inwards and upwards so that the
walls of the upper vagina contract, and squeeze the finger. If you can
do this without contracting the anus or the front part of the perineum
(clitoris and urinary opening), the location of mooladhara chakra is
correct.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 2: Moola Bandha (perineal contraction)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 1: Contraction with breath retention]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or any other posture which will
apply a firm pressure in the region of mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and relax the whole body.
:::

::: {#part0041.xhtml_page_223 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale deeply. Hold the breath and contract the muscles at the
mooladhara chakra region.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Draw the muscles upwards as much as you are able without excessive
strain.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to contract only the mooladhara chakra trigger point, so that the
urinary musculature in front and the anal sphincters behind, remain
relaxed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep your attention fixed on the exact point of contraction. Hold this
contraction for as long as possible.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then release moola bandha and breathe normally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise for a few minutes daily.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Jalandhara bandha (described
in]{.class-4} [[chapter 33]{.class-4}](#part0045.xhtml){.class5828-3}
[of this section), can also be added to the practice. With breath
retention, perform jalandhara bandha, followed by moola bandha. Before
exhaling, release moola bandha, then jalandhara bandha.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 2: Physical contraction]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Contract and release moola bandha rhythmically.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
About one contraction per second is reasonable, or if you wish, you can
synchronize the contraction with the heartbeat.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Again, ensure that the contraction is focused at the exact trigger point
and at the anus.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Direct all your attention to the point of contraction.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise for a few minutes daily.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 3: Mental contraction]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Leave all physical contraction.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to feel the pulse beat at the trigger point, or try to contract the
point mentally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Direct all your attention to the mooladhara chakra area.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The practice is similar to stage 2, without the physical contraction.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue for as long as you have time to spare.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
With practise, you will be able to locate the trigger point of
mooladhara chakra exactly, merely through thought alone.
:::

::: class1777-0
![](image1776.jpg){#page_224 .class1777-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 3: Nasikagra Drishti (nose tip gazing)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in any meditative pose with the spine erect and the head upright.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and relax the whole body for some time.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then open the eyes and focus them on the nose tip.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not strain the eyes, but try to fix the gaze on the tip of the nose.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Respiration should be normal.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When the eyes are correctly focused, a double outline of the nose is
seen.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
These two lines converge at the tip of the nose, forming an inverted
V-image.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Concentrate on the apex of the V.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If you do not see a solid V-shaped outline, then both eyes are not fixed
on the nose tip.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It is then necessary to focus the eyes on the finger tip, 25 centimetres
in front of the face, and hold the fingertip in focus as you slowly
bring it to the nose tip.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Eventually, you can discard this method and easily focus the eyes on the
nose tip at will.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At first you may find it difficult to hold your attention on the nose
tip for more than a few seconds.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you feel discomfort, release the position of the eyes for a few
seconds and then repeat the practice.
:::

::: {#part0041.xhtml_page_225 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Over a period of weeks, as the eyes become accustomed, gradually
increase the duration of the practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Never strain the eyes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Once you can comfortably maintain a steady gaze for a minute or more,
become aware of your breath as well as the nose tip.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel the breath moving in and out through the nose.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At the same time, become aware of the subtle sound the breath makes as
it moves through the nasal passages.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to become completely absorbed in the practice, to the exclusion of
all other thoughts and external distractions.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be aware of the nose tip, the movement of the breath and the
accompanying sound. Continue in this manner for up to five minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
End the practice with palming to relax and energize the eyes.
:::

::: {.class1801 lang="en-us"}
[Note]{.class5919} [: This practice is also called]{.class5827-3}
[agochari mudra]{.class-4} [(the gesture of invisibility)]{.class5827-3}
[.]{.class-4}
:::

[]{#part0042.xhtml}

::: {#part0042.xhtml_page_226 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[30](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5845)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Practices for\
Swadhisthana Chakra](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5845)
:::

::: {#part0042.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5908 .class1589 lang="en-us"}
[MONTH 3](#part0048.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5874)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[T]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} he sadhana for awakening swadhisthana chakra
is solely concerned with the uro-genital systems, the prostate gland and
testes in the male, and the genito-ovarian system in the female. Vajroli
and sahajoli mudras are two very powerful practices which rechannel
sexual energy and help bring about the awakening of swadhisthana.
Vajroli is practised by males and sahajoli by females. There are simple
forms of vajroli and also more difficult techniques which require the
direct guidance of a guru. However, the practices given here can be
performed with reasonable ease by anyone who is thoroughly familiar with
shalabhasana, dhanurasana and uddiyana bandha. Refer to 'Difference
between moola bandha, vajroli and ashwini mudras', given in [chapter
29](#part0041.xhtml) .
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Preparatory practices
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
A large number of asanas have a direct effect on swadhisthana chakra and
help to bring about initial purification and sensitization. We suggest
that you practise shakti bandha series, bhujangasana, shashankasana,
dhanurasana and shashank bhujangasana.
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice program
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
The sadhana (practices 1--4) for awakening swadhisthana chakra, should
be perfected over a period of one month. It should be kept in mind that
swadhisthana is the switch []{#part0042.xhtml_page_227} for bindu and,
therefore, the sadhana for swadhisthana also brings about a simultaneous
effect on and awakening of bindu. You can also continue the sadhana for
ajna and mooladhara chakras.
:::

::: class1412-0
![](image1817.jpg){.class1412-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1414 lang="en-us"}
Swadhisthana
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 1: Swadhisthana chakra location]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in a comfortable position. Move one finger to the lowest end of the
spine and feel the coccyx, the tailbone.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then move the finger up about one inch or 2--3 centimetres, along the
sacral portion of the pelvis, and press hard for one minute.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you take the finger away, you will experience a residual sensation.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
About one centimetre deep into that sensation is the location of
swadhisthana chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Concentrate on it for two minutes or so repeating mentally,
'swadhisthana, swadhisthana, swadhisthana'.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 2: Swadhisthana kshetram location]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If you feel down to the lower end of the abdomen, you will come to a
bony portion at the front part of the pelvis. This is called the pubis,
and is the anatomical location of swadhisthana kshetram.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Press hard on this area for about one minute.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then remove the finger and concentrate on the point where your finger
was. Repeat mentally, 'swadhisthana, swadhisthana, swadhisthana'.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 3: Ashwini Mudra (horse gesture)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in any meditative posture. Relax the whole body, close the eyes and
breathe normally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Contract the sphincter muscles of the anus for half a second, then relax
them for half a second.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue this contraction and relaxation for a few minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to feel the waves spreading up to hit swadhisthana chakra. Focus
your whole attention on the lower end of the spine and feel the pressure
waves.
:::

::: {#part0042.xhtml_page_228 .class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 4: Vajroli Mudra (thunderbolt attitude) -- for men]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit comfortably in siddhasana, preferably with a thin cushion or a
folded blanket beneath the buttocks.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and relax the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Take the awareness to the urethra, the urinary passage within the penis.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to draw the urethra upward. This muscular action is similar to that
made when trying to control the urge to urinate.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The testes may move slightly due to this contraction.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to focus and confine the force of the contraction at the urethra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try not to perform moola bandha or ashwini mudra at the same time.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Contract for 10 seconds, release for 10 seconds. Continue this for a few
minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Concentrate on the kshetram at the pubis all the time, while repeating
mentally, 'swadhisthana, swadhisthana, swadhisthana'.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 4: Sahajoli Mudra (spontaneous psychic attitude) -- for
women]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit comfortably in siddha yoni asana, preferably with a thin cushion or
folded blanket beneath the buttocks.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and relax the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Contract the urethra. This contraction is similar to that made when
trying to control the urge to urinate.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The vaginal muscles and the hood of the clitoris may move slightly due
to this contraction.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Gradually increase the contraction until it becomes more intense and
deep.
:::

::: {.class1564 lang="en-us"}
Hold the contraction for 10 seconds, release for 10 seconds. Continue
for a few minutes, mentally repeating 'swadhisthana, swadhisthana,
swadhisthana'.
:::

[]{#part0043.xhtml}

::: {#part0043.xhtml_page_229 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[31](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5936)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Practices for\
Manipura Chakra](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5936)
:::

::: {#part0043.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5877 .class1589 lang="en-us"}
[MONTH 4](#part0048.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5851)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[T]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} here are several methods of awakening
manipura chakra. According to hatha yoga, manipura is directly connected
with the eyes. Ajna chakra and manipura chakra are very closely related
to one another in the same way that vision and wilful action are
interdependent processes. Therefore, the practice of trataka brings
about manipura and ajna chakra awakening.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Although tantra is not against any particular diet, when manipura
chakra is to be awakened, the diet has to be very pure, and at certain
stages, fasting may be necessary as well. If manipura is awakened when
the diet is faulty, harmful reactions may take place. Because manipura
is the centre of the digestive fire, disorders of the gastrointestinal
system are corrected by manipura sadhana.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[The major constituents of manipura sadhana are uddiyana bandha and
nauli kriya. Uddiyana bandha is the contraction of the abdomen and the
control of the muscles of the abdominal wall, as well as control over
the small and large intestines and the other digestive and visceral
organs. The functions of the liver, gallbladder, spleen, pancreas and
stomach are brought into harmonious and controlled interaction when
uddiyana bandha is perfected. However, agnisar kriya must be mastered
before uddiyana is attempted.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Nauli kriya is the control of the rectus abdomini muscles and churning
of the whole abdomen. This is a difficult]{.class-0}
[]{#part0043.xhtml_page_230 .class-0} [practice which takes some time to
perfect. However, with mastery of nauli, it is easy to create a union of
prana and apana in the navel, so manipura chakra can be
awakened.]{.class-0}
:::

::: class1412-0
![](image1865.jpg){.class1412-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1414 lang="en-us"}
Manipura
:::

::: {.class1416 lang="en-us"}
Preparatory practices
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
The following asanas will be found useful in awakening manipura chakra:
pawanmuktasana (the anti-gastric series), chakrasana, dhanurasana,
marjari-asana, matsyasana, yoga mudra, paschimottanasana and ushtrasana.
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice program
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Practise the techniques for awakening manipura chakra for one month and
then proceed to those for anahata chakra. Nauli may be difficult for
many people; do not strain or overexert. It is best not to attempt it
until you have mastered agnisar kriya and uddiyana bandha.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[The practices for awakening ajna, mooladhara and swadhisthana can also
be continued.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 1: Manipura chakra and kshetram location]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Stand sideways in front of a mirror.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Put one finger of one hand on the navel and one finger of the other hand
on the spine, directly behind.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit down, press firmly with the finger on the spine for one minute, then
remove the finger.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As the pressure sensation continues, concentrate on the area slightly
deeper in from that point.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is the location of manipura chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Whilst feeling the pulse beat at this point, mentally repeat the mantra,
'manipura' for a few minutes.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 2: Manipura purification]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Assume a comfortable sitting pose.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold the back straight and keep the eyes closed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breathe slowly and deeply, feeling the expansion and contraction of the
navel as you breathe in and out through the navel.
:::

::: {#part0043.xhtml_page_231 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel the breath expanding and contracting in the navel area for a few
minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As the navel expands outward, feel that the breath is being pulled in
through the navel, straight back to manipura in the spine.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As the navel contracts inward, feel that the breath is flowing from
manipura chakra in the spine to the navel and out of the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise this for a few minutes each day while mentally repeating,
'manipura, manipura, manipura'.
:::

::: class1890-0
![](image1889.jpg){.class1890-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 3: Agnisar Kriya]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Preparatory practice: Swana Pranayama (panting breath)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in vajrasana. Keeping the toes together, separate the knees as far
as possible (see figure 1).
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep both hands on the knees, straighten the arms and lean forward
slightly.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Open the mouth and extend the tongue outside.
:::

::: {#part0043.xhtml_page_232 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breathe rapidly in and out while simultaneously expanding and
contracting the abdomen.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The respiration should be in harmony with the movement of the abdomen
and should resemble the panting of a dog. Breathe in and out up to 25
times.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Agnisar Kriya (activating the digestive fire)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Assume the same position (see figure 2).
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Exhale as completely as possible.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Perform jalandhara bandha.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Rapidly contract and expand the abdominal muscles repeatedly, for as
long as you are able to retain the breath outside.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Release jalandhara bandha and inhale fully.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Perform the practice 4 more times, waiting until the breath has returned
to normal between each round.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Contra-indications]{.class5829-0} [: People suffering from high blood
pressure, heart disease or acute peptic or duodenal ulcers should not
practise this kriya, nor should pregnant women or persons who have
undergone abdominal surgery in the last six to nine months.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Agnisar kriya should be practised on an
empty stomach preferably in the early in the morning before breakfast.
It should not be attempted until swana pranayama is mastered.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 4: Uddiyana Bandha (abdominal contraction)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in a siddha/siddha yoni asana or padmasana with the spine erect and
the knees touching the floor.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If this is not possible, uddiyana bandha can be performed while
standing.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Place the hands on the knees, close the eyes and relax the whole body.
Exhale completely and hold the breath outside.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Perform jalandhara bandha.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then contract the abdominal muscles as far as possible inward and
upward.
:::

::: class1916-0
![](image1915.jpg){#page_233 .class1916-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1642 lang="en-us"}
This is a kind of sucking action of the muscles.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold this lock for as long as the breath can be retained outside without
straining.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Concentrate on manipura chakra in the spine and repeat mentally,
'manipura, manipura, manipura'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Slowly relax the stomach muscles.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Release jalandhara bandha and inhale.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When the respiration has returned to normal, the process may be
repeated.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise a few rounds and gradually increase to ten.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Contra-indications]{.class5829-0} [: Same as for agnisar
kriya.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 5: Nauli (abdominal massaging)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 1: Madhyama Nauli (central abdominal contraction)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Stand with the feet about a metre apart.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Take a deep breath in through the nose and then exhale through the
mouth, emptying the lungs as much as possible.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bend the knees slightly and lean forward, placing the palms on the
thighs just above the knees, so that the knees are supporting the weight
of the body. The arms should remain straight.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Perform jalandhara bandha while retaining the breath outside.
:::

::: class1934-1
![](image1933.jpg){#page_234 .class1934-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1642 lang="en-us"}
Keep the eyes open and watch the abdomen.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Suck in the lower abdomen.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Contract the rectus abdomini muscles so that they form a central arch
running vertically in front of the abdomen.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold the contraction for as long as it is comfortable to hold the
breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Release the contraction, raise the head and return to the upright
position. Inhale slowly and deeply, allowing the abdomen to expand.
Relax the whole body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is one round. Relax in the standing position until the heartbeat
returns to normal. Repeat the practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Madhyama nauli should be perfected before proceeding to the next stage.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 2: Vama Nauli (left isolation)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Follow the instructions for madhyama nauli to the point where the lower
abdomen is contracted and the rectus abdomini muscles form a central,
vertical arch down the abdomen.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Isolate the rectus abdomini muscles at the left side.
:::

::: class1948-0
![](image1947.jpg){#page_235 .class1948-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1642 lang="en-us"}
Contract the muscles to the left side as strongly as possible without
straining.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Return to madhyama nauli.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Release the abdominal contraction, raise the head and return to the
upright position.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale slowly and deeply, allowing the abdomen to expand.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is one round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Relax in the upright position until the heartbeat returns to normal.
Proceed to stage 3.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 3: Dakshina Nauli (right isolation)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After completing vama nauli, practise in the same way but on the right
side.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Follow the instructions for madhyama nauli to the point where the lower
abdomen is contracted and the rectus abdomini muscles form a central,
vertical arch down the abdomen.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Isolate the rectus abdomini muscles at the right side.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold the contraction as tightly as possible while retaining the breath.
:::

::: {#part0043.xhtml_page_236 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not strain. Return to madhyama nauli.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Release the abdominal contraction, raise the head and return to the
upright position.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale slowly and deeply, allowing the abdomen to expand.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is one round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Relax in the upright position until the heartbeat returns to normal.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Proceed to abdominal rotation or churning only after perfecting this
practice.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 4: Abdominal rotation or churning]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This practice should not be attempted until the previous three stages
have been mastered.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise vama nauli, then rotate the muscles to the right, dakshina
nauli, and back to the left, vama nauli.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue rotating the muscles from side to side. This process is known
as churning.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Start by practising 3 consecutive rotations, then release the abdominal
contraction.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Next start with dakshina nauli first, this time rotating the muscles
from right to left, left to right 3 times consecutively.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then perform madhyama nauli, isolating the muscles at the centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Raise the head and return to the upright position.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale slowly and deeply, allowing the abdomen to expand.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is one round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Relax in the upright position until the heartbeat returns to normal.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise each round for as long as the breath can be retained.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do up to six 6 rounds.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Contra-indications]{.class5829-0} [: Limitations are the same as for
agnisar kriya.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Nauli should not be attempted until
agnisar kriya and uddiyana bandha have been perfected.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {#part0043.xhtml_page_237 .class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 6: Union of prana and apana]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana or siddha yoni asana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Relax the whole body for a few minutes, bringing it to the point of
absolute immobility.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now become aware of the natural abdominal breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Centre the awareness on the movement of the navel as you inhale and
exhale.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue for a few minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now become aware that there are two forces travelling to the navel --
prana and apana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
One force (apana) is ascending from mooladhara to the navel, while the
other (prana), is descending to the navel from above. They must both
reach the navel at the point of full inhalation. When you feel that the
two forces are meeting in the navel, perform kumbhaka, retention of
breath, and then develop mental awareness of the single central point of
force in the navel.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not strain.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Release the breath and continue this practice in your own natural
rhythm.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The awareness of the two forces travelling and meeting in the navel
centre must be simultaneous.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now, as the two forces are converging in the navel, gradually allow
moola bandha to take place.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Go on contracting moola bandha as you heighten your awareness of the
force which is centred in the navel.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold your breath for as long as you can, while centralizing the force in
the navel and performing moola bandha.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you release the breath, release moola bandha as well.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not strain.
:::

::: {.class1564 lang="en-us"}
Go on practising for 3 minutes or more.
:::

[]{#part0044.xhtml}

::: {#part0044.xhtml_page_238 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[32](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5930)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Practices for\
Anahata Chakra](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5930)
:::

::: {#part0044.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5867 .class1589 lang="en-us"}
[MONTH 5](#part0048.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5967)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[A]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} nahata chakra can be awakened very simply
through the practice of ajapa japa. Japa means 'repetition' and ajapa is
the repetition of a mantra until it ultimately becomes the spontaneous
form of your conscious awareness.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Another important practice in anahata awakening is bhramari pranayama.
Although it is called a pranayama, bhramari is actually a meditational
practice. It is not directly related to controlling prana, as are other
forms of pranayama. In the scriptures, the heart centre is termed 'the
centre of unstruck sound' and also 'the cave of bees'. In bhramari, the
humming sound of the bees is produced and traced towards its source.
This develops deep mental and emotional relaxation and is extremely
effective in cardiac disorders.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Anahata chakra is the centre of bhakti or devotion. It is awakened in
accordance with the degree of devotion to guru, God, or personal deity,
in whatever form or non-form one may visualize or understand the
spiritual intelligence of the universe. All practices of yoga,
especially when done with the blessings of the guru, will automatically
awaken devotion in the spiritual heart (anahata chakra). There are many
excellent books on bhakti yoga that will help to inspire the aspirant to
follow this path. Any biographies of saints, yogis and bhaktas will also
be useful. An excellent description of the process of bhakti yoga is
given in our publication entitled,]{.class-0} [A Systematic Course in
the Ancient Tantric Techniques of Yoga and Kriya]{.class5827-1} [, and
in]{.class-0} [Bhakti Yoga Sagar]{.class5827-1} [, Volumes 1--5, by
Swami Satyananda Saraswati.]{.class-0}
:::

::: class1412-0
![](image2011.jpg){.class1412-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1414 lang="en-us"}
Anahata
:::

::: {#part0044.xhtml_page_239 .class1416 lang="en-us"}
Practice program
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Practise these techniques for anahata chakra for one month and then
begin those for awakening vishuddhi chakra. All the practices given for
awakening ajna, mooladhara, swadhisthana and manipura chakras can be
done if sufficient time is available. If not, then we suggest that you
do a few selected techniques from each chakra sadhana as follows:
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[1.]{.class-1} [Ajna]{.class5827-2} [-- trataka and shambhavi
mudra]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[2.]{.class-1} [Mooladhara]{.class5827-2} [-- moola bandha and nasikagra
mudra]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[3.]{.class-1} [Swadhisthana]{.class5827-2} [-- chakra and kshetram
location, vajroli or sahajoli]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[4.]{.class-1} [Manipura]{.class5827-2} [-- chakra and kshetram
location, uddiyana bandha and nauli (if possible).]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 1: Anahata chakra and kshetram location]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Stand sideways in front of a mirror.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Put one finger of one hand on the centre of the chest.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Here you will find anahata kshetram.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Put one finger of the other hand on the spine, directly behind the
kshetram; this is anahata chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit down, press both fingers firmly for one minute, and then remove the
fingers.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The sensation at the chakra and kshetram will continue.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Concentrate on the sensation at the chakra and mentally repeat,
'anahata, anahata, anahata', for a few minutes.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 2: Anahata purification]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Assume a comfortable sitting posture. Hold the back straight but without
strain. Keep the eyes closed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breathe slowly and deeply, feeling the expansion and contraction of the
chest as you breathe in and out for some minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then become aware of the breath moving in and out of the anahata region.
:::

::: {#part0044.xhtml_page_240 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
As the chest expands, feel that the breath flows in through the centre
of the chest and back to anahata chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As the chest contracts, feel that the breath flows from anahata chakra
in the spine, through the centre of the chest and out of the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise this for some minutes, mentally repeating, 'anahata, anahata,
anahata'.
:::

::: class2038-1
![](image2037.jpg){.class2038-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 3: Bhramari Pranayama (humming bee breath)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in a comfortable meditative pose. Adjust your position and relax
fully for some minutes. Face forward.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold the head and spine as straight as possible.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Relax the whole body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep the teeth slightly separated and the mouth closed throughout the
entire practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This allows the vibration to be experienced more distinctly in the
brain.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Plug the ears with the index fingers.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breathe in slowly and deeply.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then, while breathing out, produce a humming sound.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The sound should be smooth and continuous for the full duration of
exhalation.
:::

::: {#part0044.xhtml_page_241 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
The humming need not be loud.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The important thing is that you hear the sound reverberating within your
head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The exhalation should be slow and controlled.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At the end of exhalation, stop the humming sound and breathe in fully.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep the eyes closed and the ears plugged.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Again repeat the humming sound with the next exhalation.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to relax fully during the practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not strain in any way.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue for 5 or 10 minutes.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 4: Ajapa japa meditation]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana, siddha yoni asana or any posture which feels
completely comfortable.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and relax for a few minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now become aware of the natural breath as it enters and leaves the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not try to control the breath, just become a witness of the natural
breathing process.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now become aware that the sound of inhalation is [So]{.class5827-0} and
the sound of exhalation is [ham]{.class5827-0} . The natural mantra of
the breath is [So-ham]{.class5827-0} . You have only to discover it.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be simultaneously aware of the natural breath, coupled with the idea of
[So-ham-so-ham-so-ham.]{.class5827-0}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
You must be totally relaxed in this practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not lose awareness of the mantra or your natural breath, even for an
instant. Do not be concerned with the thoughts and feelings that arise.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Allow them to come and go as they will. Remain ever aware of the natural
breath and the ongoing mantra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now become aware of the psychic breath which is flowing in an imaginary
or psychic passage in the front of the body between the navel and the
throat, and between the throat and the navel.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
With inspiration, this psychic breath rises from the navel to throat and
its mantra is [So]{.class5827-0} . With expiration, the psychic
[]{#part0044.xhtml_page_242} breath descends from the throat back to the
navel. Its mantra is [ham]{.class5827-0} .
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Maintain awareness of the breath passing through the psychic passageway
and producing the sound [So-ham-so-ham-so-ham.]{.class5827-0}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue this practice for 10 or 15 minutes more, allowing your
breathing to be totally relaxed.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Ajapa japa can be practised at any
time, but it should be done for 5 to 10 minutes per day, either in the
morning sadhana session or at night, immediately before sleep. It should
be continued for at least one month.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 5: Meditation -- entering the heart space]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 1: Breath awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana, siddha yoni asana or any other comfortable posture.
Close the eyes and relax completely for some time. Concentrate the
awareness in the throat region.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now become aware of the breath in the throat.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Only be aware of the sensation of the breath in the throat for some
time.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now add the awareness of the ingoing breath from the throat downwards.
You are not concerned with the outgoing breath. Your attention is
occupied only with the ingoing breath in the throat.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of the inflowing breath in the throat passing within the
network of the diaphragm.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be aware of the diaphragm -- the rising and falling of the muscular
floor separating the chest and lungs above from the abdominal organs
below.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
With each inspiration, it drops into the abdomen a little, increasing
the pressure there and causing the navel to expand.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Simultaneously, the lungs are expanding fully in the chest.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be aware that with expiration the abdomen contracts, the diaphragm is
rising and the lungs are emptying completely.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Develop awareness of the diaphragm for some time.
:::

::: {#part0044.xhtml_page_243 .class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 2: Awareness of the heart space]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now, also become aware of the akasha, the space within which the
diaphragm is operating.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
With the ingoing breath you feel this space is filling up.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Only be aware of the process of filling up the space.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This process of filling up is only a basis for the awareness of this
vast space.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The process of feeling the breath is only the basis for experiencing the
heart space.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of the space in the heart; take your awareness directly
there.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel the space within the heart centre. It is contracting and expanding
with the rhythm of the natural breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breath is only the basis.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The process of filling up is only the basis.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Go on to comprehend the whole space.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then you are aware of the space alone.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel the contraction and expansion of this vast space.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It is taking place on the rhythm of the natural breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The breath is natural and spontaneous.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not alter it in any way.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not make it longer or shorter, deeper or more shallow, faster or
slower.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It has to become a spontaneous and voluntary movement of breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
In this practice, the awareness of the space in the heart is important.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 3: Vision of blue lotus and lake]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If the awareness of the expansion and contraction of the heart space is
constant and stabilized, after some time, many visions and experiences
will manifest there.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
You do not have to visualize or imagine anything. The vision will come
by itself when the awareness of the heart space is constant.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The image is of a lake and a blue lotus.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If you are able to feel the space of the heart contracting and
expanding, then maintain your awareness there.
:::

::: {#part0044.xhtml_page_244 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
If that is not possible, then you will have to feel the breath which is
filling up the space. That is the first stage of the practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The second stage is the direct feeling of the space and its expansion
and contraction with the rhythm of the breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The third stage is the awareness of the blue lotus and the still lake.
It will come by itself.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep yourself ready for that experience.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 4: Ending the practice]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now become aware of the natural inflowing and outflowing breath in the
throat.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Withdraw your awareness from the heart space and bring it to the natural
breath in the throat.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Maintain awareness of the inflowing and outflowing breath in the throat
for some time.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise for five or ten minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Chant Om three times.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Allow the sound to manifest fully and spontaneously from deep within.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
For a few minutes, listen carefully for the inner vibration of the
sound.
:::

::: {.class1564 lang="en-us"}
Release your posture and open your eyes.
:::

[]{#part0045.xhtml}

::: {#part0045.xhtml_page_245 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[33](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5838)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Practices for\
Vishuddhi Chakra](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5838)
:::

::: {#part0045.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5852 .class1589 lang="en-us"}
[MONTH 6](#part0048.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5988)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[V]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} ishuddhi chakra can be directly awakened
through the practices of jalandhara bandha, vipareeta karani asana and
ujjayi pranayama, all of which are essential for eventual mastery of
kriya yoga.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[A minor chakra which is closely related to vishuddhi is called lalana
chakra, which is located at the back of the roof of the mouth, at the
soft palate, and it directly helps to awaken vishuddhi. For this reason,
one of the kundalini kriyas, called amrit pan, is concerned with its
direct stimulation. A simpler practice for awakening lalana is khechari
mudra, which is described in this chapter.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Preparatory practices
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Many asanas can be utilized for purifying vishuddhi chakra. The most
important are: bhujangasana, matsyasana, supta vajrasana and
sarvangasana.
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice program
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Perfect these vishuddhi chakra practices over a period of one month and
then start the practices for bindu. The sadhana for the other chakras
can also be continued with a few selected techniques from each of the
other chakras as follows:
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[1.]{.class-1} [Ajna]{.class5827-2} [-- trataka and shambhavi
mudra]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[2.]{.class-1} [Mooladhara]{.class5827-2} [-- moola bandha and nasikagra
mudra]{.class-1}
:::

::: {#part0045.xhtml_page_246 .class2016 lang="en-us"}
[3.]{.class-1} [Swadhisthana]{.class5827-2} [-- chakra and kshetram
location, vajroli or sahajoli.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[4.]{.class-1} [Manipura]{.class5827-2} [-- chakra and kshetram
location, uddiyana bandha and nauli.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[5.]{.class-1} [Anahata]{.class5827-2} [-- chakra and kshetram location,
ajapa japa.]{.class-1}
:::

::: class1412-0
![](image2144.jpg){.class1412-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1414 lang="en-us"}
Vishuddhi
:::

::: class2149-1
![](image2148.jpg){.class2149-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 1: Jalandhara Bandha (throat lock)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in any meditative pose which allows the knees to firmly touch the
floor. Those who cannot sit like this can practise jalandhara bandha in
a standing position.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Place the palms of the hands on the knees.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and relax the whole body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale deeply, retain the breath inside and bend the head forward,
pressing the chin tightly against the chest (particularly the sternum).
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Straighten the arms and lock them into position.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Simultaneously hunch the shoulders upward and forward. This will ensure
that the arms remain locked.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The palms should remain on the knees.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Stay in the final pose for as long as the breath can be held
comfortably.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then bend the arms, relax the shoulders, slowly release the lock, raise
the head and exhale.
:::

::: {#part0045.xhtml_page_247 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat when the respiration returns to normal.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise 5 times.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Contra-indications]{.class5829-0} [: Persons with high intracranial or
blood pressure, or with heart ailments, should not practise without
expert guidance.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: The whole practice can also be
performed with the breath retained outside.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Never inhale or exhale until the chin lock has been released and the
head is upright.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 2: Khechari Mudra (tongue lock)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in a comfortable meditative posture.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the mouth and roll the tongue upward and backward so that the
lower surface touches the upper palate. Stretch the tip of the tongue as
far back as possible without strain.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep it there for as long as is comfortable.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If there is discomfort, relax the tongue for a few seconds and repeat.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After some practise the tongue may be able to extend beyond the palate
and up into the nasopharynx, where it will stimulate many vital nerve
centres.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Breathing]{.class5829-0} [: Breathe normally during this practice
unless ujjayi is used.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Duration]{.class5829-0} [: Over a period of months gradually reduce the
breathing rate to seven or eight breaths per minute. This may be reduced
further under expert guidance.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 3: Ujjayi Pranayama (psychic breath)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in a comfortable meditative posture.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise khechari mudra. Feel that the breath is being drawn in and out
through the throat, not the nostrils.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Gently contract the glottis in the throat.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you breathe under these circumstances, a very soft snoring sound
should automatically come from the throat region. It is like the
breathing of a sleeping baby.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel that you are breathing deeply from the abdomen and not the nose.
:::

::: {#part0045.xhtml_page_248 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to make the breaths long and relaxed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
