Practise for two minutes initially, then gradually extend to ten or
twenty minutes.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 4: Vishuddhi chakra and kshetram location and
purification]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit or stand in front of a mirror.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Place a finger of one hand on the glottis (the lump at the throat pit).
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is the location point of vishuddhi kshetram.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then place a finger of the other hand on the spine, directly behind the
kshetram.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This point in the spine is called vishuddhi chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Press the spine for one minute in order to feel a sensation at the
chakra area.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then lower the hands.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Concentrate on the sensation at the chakra and repeat mentally,
'Vishuddhi, vishuddhi, vishuddhi'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in a comfortable position with the back straight.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and become aware of the breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Fold the tongue back into khechari mudra and practise ujjayi pranayama.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
For a minute or so, be aware of the sound of the breath at the throat,
and let the breathing become slower and deeper.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then with inhalation, imagine that the breath is being drawn in through
vishuddhi kshetram at the front of the throat.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel that the breath passes through the kshetram and eventually pierces
vishuddhi chakra in the spine.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
With exhalation, feel the breath move from vishuddhi chakra, forward
through the kshetram and eventually out, in front of the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is one round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue for a few minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Daily practise in this manner will gradually develop sensitivity to
vishuddhi chakra and its kshetram.
:::

::: class2203-1
![](image2202.jpg){#page_249 .class2203-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 5: Vipareeta Karani Asana (inverted pose)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Lie flat on the floor with the feet together, the arms by the sides and
the palms flat on the floor.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Relax the whole body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Raise both legs, keeping them straight and together.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Move the legs over the body towards the head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Push down on the arms and hands, raising the buttocks.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Roll the spine from the floor, taking the legs over the head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Turn the palms up, bend the elbows and let the top of the hips rest on
the base of the palms near the wrist.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The hands cup the hips and support the weight of the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep the elbows as close to each other as possible.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Raise both the legs to the vertical position and relax the feet.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
In the final position, the weight of the body rests on the shoulders,
neck and elbows, the trunk is at a 45 degree
[]{#part0045.xhtml_page_250} angle to the floor and the legs are
vertical. Note that the chin does not press against the chest.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and relax in the final pose for as long as is
comfortable.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
To return to the starting position, slowly lower the spine, vertebra by
vertebra, along the floor.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not lift the head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When the buttocks reach the floor, lower the legs, keeping them
straight.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Relax in shavasana.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Duration]{.class5829-0} [: Advanced practitioners can hold the posture
for 15 minutes or even more, Beginners should practise for a few seconds
and add a few seconds daily.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Sequence]{.class5829-0} [: Shavasana should be done for a few minutes
on completion of vipareeta karani asana, followed by a counterpose such
as saral matsyasana.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Contra-indications]{.class5829-0} [: This asana should not be done by
sufferers of thyroid, liver or spleen enlargement, high blood pressure
or heart ailments.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Vipareeta karani asana is similar to
sarvangasana, except that the chin is not pressed against the chest and
the trunk is held at a 45 degree angle to the ground instead of at right
angles.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1801 lang="en-us"}
[Note]{.class5919} [: Vipareeta karani asana is widely used in kriya
yoga since it helps to redirect the energies of the body from the lower
to the higher chakras. It is an integral part of the first of the
kundalini kriyas called]{.class5827-3} [vipareeta karani
mudra.]{.class-4}
:::

[]{#part0046.xhtml}

::: {#part0046.xhtml_page_251 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[34](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5933)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Practices for\
Bindu](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5933)
:::

::: {#part0046.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5844 .class1589 lang="en-us"}
[MONTH 7](#part0048.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5878)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[T]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} he bindu trigger point is considered to be a
tiny point at the top of the back of the head, but this point cannot be
located in the physical body. It can only be found when the nada or
sound of bindu has been discovered and traced to its source. Through the
practices of [moorchha pranayama]{.class5827-0} and [vajroli/sahajoli
mudra]{.class5827-0} awareness of the nada can be developed. Then,
through practices such as [bhramari pranayama]{.class5827-0} and
[shanmukhi mudra]{.class5827-0} , the nada can be traced to its source.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[It is not intended that you practise all the nada yoga techniques at
one time. You should adopt the practice which you can perform without
difficulty. It does not matter which practice you commence with, because
all the techniques lead to awareness of the same subtle inner
sounds.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[There is a very close relationship between swadhisthana chakra and
bindu. This is because bindu is the point where the primal sound of
creation first manifests. It is the point of origin of individuality,
and swadhisthana is the source of the impetus towards reproduction and
sexual function. This is the material expression of the desire to
reunite with the infinite consciousness beyond bindu. Sperm and menses
are the material distillates of the drop of ambrosial nectar which
emerges from bindu.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[It should be noted that there is no kshetram corresponding to
bindu.]{.class-0}
:::

::: class1412-0
![](image2240.jpg){.class1412-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1414 lang="en-us"}
Bindu
:::

::: {#part0046.xhtml_page_252 .class1416 lang="en-us"}
Practice program
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Practise the techniques for bindu for one month. Then begin the
techniques given in the next chapter for integrated chakra awareness.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[The selected techniques for ajna, mooladhara, swadhisthana, manipura
and anahata chakras can also be done daily, as given in the 'Practice
program' section of the previous chapter. For vishuddhi chakra,
jalandhara bandha, vishuddhi chakra purification and vipareeta karani
asana can be done. Khechari mudra and ujjayi pranayama need not be done
separately, since they are both incorporated into techniques given in
this section.]{.class-0}
:::

::: class2248-0
![](image2247.jpg){.class2248-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 1: Moorchha Pranayama (swooning or fainting breath)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This practice requires a steady and firm meditation posture, preferably
siddhasana or siddha yoni asana. Hold the spine and head upright and
relax the whole body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Perform khechari mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale through the nostrils with ujjayi pranayama while simultaneously
bending the head backward and assuming shambhavi mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The inhalation should be slow and deep.
:::

::: {#part0046.xhtml_page_253 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
At the end of inhalation, the head should lean backward, but not
completely. The position of the head is as shown in the diagram. Retain
the breath inside for as long as is comfortable, maintaining shambhavi
mudra, but keeping the attention at bindu.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep the arms straight by locking the elbows and pressing the knees with
the hands.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Fix your whole awareness on bindu.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then bend the arms and slowly exhale with ujjayi pranayama as you bend
the head forward. Slowly lower and close the eyes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At the end of exhalation the head should face forward and the eyes
should be completely closed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Relax the whole body for a short time, keeping the eyes closed. Release
khechari mudra and breathe normally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of the lightness and calmness pervading the whole mind.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is one round. After some time, commence the second round.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Duration]{.class5829-0} [: Practise 10 or more rounds, or until a
fainting sensation is experienced. Perform each round for as long as
possible, but without strain.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Contra-indications]{.class5829-0} [: Those who suffer from high blood
pressure, vertigo, high intracranial pressure or brain haemorrhage
should not practise this technique. Discontinue the practice as soon as
the fainting sensation is felt. The aim is to induce a state of
semi-fainting, not complete unconsciousness.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Benefits]{.class5829-0} [: This practice is very powerful in inducing
pratyahara and rendering the mind free from thoughts, especially when
kumbhaka is prolonged.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 2: Vajroli/sahajoli mudra with awareness of bindu]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana or siddha yoni asana, preferably with a thin cushion
or a folded blanket beneath the buttocks.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and relax the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Take the awareness to the urethra.
:::

::: {#part0046.xhtml_page_254 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Contract the urethra as if it is being drawn upwards and inwards.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This muscular action is similar to that made when trying to control the
urge to urinate.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to focus and confine the force of the contraction at the urethra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try not to perform moola bandha or ashwini mudra at the same time.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Contract for 10 seconds, release for 10 seconds. Continue this for a few
minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Each time you attain full contraction of the urinary system, bring your
awareness to swadhisthana chakra in the spinal column, at the level of
the coccyx. Repeat, 'Swadhisthana, swadhisthana, swadhisthana',
mentally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then draw your awareness up through sushumna passage to bindu.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Mentally repeat, 'bindu, bindu, bindu'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then return to swadhisthana and release vajroli/sahajoli mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is one round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue this alternately for several minutes, practising up to 25
rounds.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: This practice should be performed
immediately after moorchha pranayama, as both these practices awaken the
awareness of bindu.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 3: Perception of subtle inner sound]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This practice should be preceded by bhramari pranayama.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
In this stage no loud humming sound is produced, you only listen
attentively to the inner sound.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep the eyes closed and the fingers plugging the ears; this is
necessary to block out external disturbances.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Listen for any subtle sounds in the head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At first you may find this difficult, but keep trying.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As soon as you become aware of a sound, any sound, try to fix your
awareness on it to the exclusion of other sounds.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Go on listening.
:::

::: {#part0046.xhtml_page_255 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
After some days or weeks of practice, you should find that one sound is
very distinct, and it will become louder and louder.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be totally aware of that sound.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is your vehicle of awareness -- let your awareness flow towards
this sound, leaving all other sounds and thoughts.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Gradually, through practise, your sensitivity will increase.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Eventually you will hear another sound, a faint sound in the background;
it will be almost obliterated by the main, louder sound that you are
hearing, but you will hear it nevertheless.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now listen to the new faint sound.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Leave the other louder sound and continue to listen to the new sound. It
will become more and more distinct.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This will become your new, more subtle vehicle of awareness.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Let this sound occupy your whole attention. This will further increase
your sensitivity of perception.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Eventually you will hear another faint sound emerging from behind this
louder sound.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Fix your awareness on this new sound, discarding the other sound.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue in the same manner, allowing the new sound to occupy your whole
awareness.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When it becomes loud, try to perceive a more subtle underlying sound and
fix your awareness on it.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
In this manner your perception will become progressively more sensitive,
allowing you to dive deep into your being.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: It requires practise over a period of
weeks and months to perceive these progressively more subtle sounds. For
many weeks you may be unable to hear even the first sound.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is a very simple but powerful technique that will bring results if
you persevere. All that is necessary is time and effort. Try to practise
for as long as you have time. Begin with 15 minutes or more of bhramari
and this practice together.
:::

::: class2308-0
![](image2307.jpg){#page_256 .class2308-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Practice 4: Shanmukhi Mudra (closing the seven gates)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana, if possible. Otherwise take a
comfortable meditation asana and place a small cushion beneath the
perineum to provide pressure in this area. Hold the head and spine
straight.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and place the hands on the knees.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Completely relax the body and mind.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Raise the hands in front of the face, with the elbows pointing sideways.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the ears with the thumbs, the eyes with the index fingers, the
nostrils with the middle fingers, and the mouth by placing the ring and
little fingers above and below the lips.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The fingers should gently but firmly close the seven doors.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Release the pressure of the middle fingers and open the nostrils.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale slowly and deeply, using full yogic breathing.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At the end of inhalation, close the nostrils with the middle fingers.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Retain the breath for as long as is comfortable.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to hear any sounds emanating from bindu at the back of the head,
from the middle of the head, or perhaps the right ear.
:::

::: {#part0046.xhtml_page_257 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
At first you will either hear many sounds or none at all. Just continue
listening.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Retain the breath inside for as long as is comfortable.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then release the pressure of the middle fingers and slowly breathe out.
This is one round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale once more, close the nostrils, and retain the breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Listen to the inner sounds.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After a comfortable length of time, release the nostrils and breathe
out. Continue in this way for the duration of the practice. During the
period of breath retention, your full awareness should be directed to
the perception of inner nada.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At first there may be a confused jumble of sounds, but gradually you
will hear a specific sound. This may take a few days or weeks, but it
will be perceived.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you hear a distinct sound, be totally aware of it.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It will become clearer and clearer. Keep your awareness fixed on the
sound. Listen very carefully.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If your sensitivity is sufficiently developed, you will hear another
sound in the background. It may be faint, but perceptible.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Leave the first sound and transfer your awareness to the perception of
the fainter sound.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
In this way, you will transcend the first sound. Eventually this second
sound will overwhelm your whole attention.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Again, with practise and enhanced sensitivity, you will hear a further
sound start to emerge. It will be faintly perceptible behind the louder
second sound.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Direct your awareness to this new sound.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Carry on in this way -- perceive a sound and then discard it when you
can hear a more subtle sound. The more subtle the sound you perceive,
the deeper you will delve into the depth of your being.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue this practice for a few minutes.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Breathing]{.class5829-0} [: This technique is more effective if you can
retain your breath for extended periods of time. Those aspirants who
have been practising nadi shodhana pranayama]{.class-4}
[]{#part0046.xhtml_page_258 .class-4} [regularly for some months
beforehand, will find shanmukhi mudra an easy and effective means of
introspection.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Awareness]{.class5829-0} [: The point of awareness during the practice
should be fixed at the back of the head in the bindu region. However, if
you hear a distinct sound in any other area, such as the right ear or
the middle of the head, then your awareness should be fixed
there.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Some people may find it easier to listen to the nada in the region of
the heart space (anahata chakra), especially those of a devotional
nature. The important thing is not so much the point of awareness, but
that the awareness remains fixed on progressively more subtle sounds.
Total absorption on the nada can lead to dhyana or the meditative state
of awareness.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Do not expect to hear subtle sounds on
your first attempt. Practice is necessary. Eventually you will be able
to readily transcend the gross external sounds and then the
progressively more subtle sounds. Do not dwell on any of the sounds for
too long. This is not the purpose of the practice. The aim is to leave
behind each sound you discover and to go deeper, to reach the source of
all sound. Do not get lost or distracted by the beautiful sounds which
will manifest on your journey.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Shanmukhi mudra is a more advanced practice than bhramari. It is
slightly more difficult as it is not preceded by a vocalized humming
sound, and it is combined with retention of the breath. Shanmukhi mudra
is suitable for those who have a reasonably harmonized mind and are not
beset by distractions.
:::

::: {.class1801 lang="en-us"}
[Note]{.class5919} [:]{.class5827-3} [Shanmukhi mudra]{.class-4} [means
'the closing of the seven gates'. It is so called because the two eyes,
two ears, two nostrils and the mouth are closed during the practice.
These are the seven doors of outer perception. It is via these doorways
that one receives the sense data from the outside world. When these
doors are closed, we facilitate the direction of the awareness
internally; that is, into the mind.]{.class5827-3}
:::

[]{#part0047.xhtml}

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_259 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[35](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5886)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Practices for Integrated\
Chakra Awareness](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5886)
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5863 .class1589 lang="en-us"}
[MONTH 8](#part0048.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5948)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[S]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} o far we have given a series of practices for
each of the individual chakras. In this chapter we will describe
practices which are concerned with the overall awakening of the chakras.
Of course, the awakening of one chakra cannot take place in isolation;
it has repercussions on all the chakras to a greater or lesser extent.
The techniques for specific chakras will also influence all the chakras,
but the following techniques systematically help to activate all the
chakras together and bring balance into the whole mind-body-chakra axis:
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[1. Chakra meditation]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[2. Musical chakra meditation]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[3. Chaturtha pranayama]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[4. Chakra yoga nidra]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[5. Unmani mudra]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[6. Beeja mantra sanchalana]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[7. Drawing the chakras]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice program
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
You will not have time to do all the practices given in this chapter.
Therefore, we suggest that you practise the following for one month:
Chakra meditation, chaturtha pranayama, chakra yoga nidra, unmani mudra
and beeja mantra sanchalana daily.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Musical chakra meditation and drawing the chakras, can be done if you
have the time and the inclination. They can]{.class-0}
[]{#part0047.xhtml_page_260 .class-0} [be omitted without any detriment
to arousing kundalini. The following practices for each individual
chakra can be done:]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[1.]{.class-1} [Ajna]{.class5827-2} [-- shambhavi mudra]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[2.]{.class-1} [Mooladhara]{.class5827-2} [-- moola bandha and nasikagra
mudra]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[3.]{.class-1} [Swadhisthana]{.class5827-2} [--
vajroli/sahajoli]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[4.]{.class-1} [Manipura]{.class5827-2} [-- uddiyana bandha]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[5.]{.class-1} [Anahata]{.class5827-2} [-- ajapa japa]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[6.]{.class-1} [Vishuddhi]{.class5827-2} [-- jalandhara bandha and
vipareeta karani asana]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[7.]{.class-1} [Bindu]{.class5827-2} [-- shanmukhi mudra]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[After one month you can start to learn kriya yoga, having first of all
obtained the advice of an experienced yoga teacher, or by writing to
Bihar School of Yoga, Munger, Bihar -- 811201, India.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice 1: Chakra meditation
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
For the purpose of practising kriya yoga and some of the more advanced
forms of meditation, it is essential to develop subtle awareness of the
chakras, and to be able to locate them all accurately. In the beginning
most people do not actually experience any sensation and initially it is
simply a matter of imagination, but as the awareness becomes more
subtle, the pulsation will definitely be experienced.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Technique]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 1: Preparation]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Make yourself comfortable in a meditative asana, preferably siddhasana
or siddha yoni asana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Place both hands on the knees in chin mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and make the whole body still and steady throughout.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The spinal column should be absolutely upright and straight, with the
back and shoulders fully relaxed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The head should be poised comfortably on top of the spinal column.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The whole body is completely relaxed and immobile.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It is motionless like a statue.
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_261 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Maintain absolute awareness of the physical body for several minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 2: Ajna awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of the spinal column.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now bring your awareness to ajna chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Ajna chakra is located inside the brain at a point directly behind the
eyebrow centre and on top of the spinal column, where the pineal gland
is situated.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to discover a pulsation within this ajna chakra region.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be absolutely aware of this pulsation.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now synchronize the mantra [Om]{.class5827-0} with the pulsation in the
ajna chakra region.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
[Om, Om, Om, Om, Om]{.class5827-0} should be the form of your awareness
with the pulsation of ajna chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Count the pulsation 21 times.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now begin to practise ashwini mudra, contraction and relaxation of the
anus.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not be concerned with ajna chakra, only practise ashwini mudra. It
should be practised at a medium speed, neither too quickly nor too
slowly.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After practising like this for a few sessions, you should be able to
feel the centre of ajna automatically while performing ashwini.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When that happens you can begin to concentrate directly on ajna.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Until then, practise ashwini mudra for about four minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 3: Mooladhara awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now bring your awareness to the perineal region and the psychic centre
of mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Discover the precise psychic point of mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to discover a subtle pulsation there.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Localize the pulsation very precisely in the mooladhara region and count
21 pulsations.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now open your eyes and adopt nasikagra drishti; gazing at the nose tip.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not be concerned with mooladhara chakra, but only with nose tip
awareness.
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_262 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
The simultaneous awareness of mooladhara chakra will come after some
time.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue this practice for three minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 4: Swadhisthana awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now bring your awareness to swadhisthana chakra in the region of the
tailbone.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Discover the psychic point of swadhisthana chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to discover the pulsation in this centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Count this pulsation 21 times.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now perform vajroli/sahajoli mudra -- the drawing up and releasing of
the urinary system.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue vajroli/sahajoli mudra for four minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 5: Manipura awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now bring your awareness to the region of the navel.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of the psychic breath in the frontal passage from
mooladhara to the navel, and from the throat to the navel.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Both these breaths must reach the navel at the point of full inhalation.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When the two forces meet and coincide at the navel, retain the breath
there, and develop the mental awareness of the single central point of
force in the navel.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then release the breath and continue this practice in your own natural
rhythm.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue for four minutes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now take your awareness directly back to manipura chakra, within the
spinal column, directly behind the navel.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to isolate that point and the pulsation there.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Count the pulse 21 times in manipura chakra.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 6: Anahata awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now bring your awareness to the region of anahata chakra in the spinal
column, at the level of the centre of the chest.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Isolate that point and try to discover a pulsation within it.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Count the pulsation 21 times.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now bring your awareness to the space of the heart.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
First become aware of the incoming breath in the throat.
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_263 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
With the incoming breath, feel the vast heart space expand.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel the heart space directly -- contracting and expanding with the
rhythm of the spontaneous, natural breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be aware of the vision which will come in the vast heart space. Allow it
to come by itself.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue for two minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 7: Vishuddhi awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now bring your awareness to the throat pit and then take it directly
back to vishuddhi chakra in the spinal column.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'Vishuddhi, vishuddhi, vishuddhi'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to discover the pulsation within vishuddhi and witness it for 21
pulsations.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 8: Chakra awareness in sushumna]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now, as the name of each chakra is given, move your awareness within the
sushumna passage so as to touch each chakra mentally with a small
imaginary flower.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Your awareness of each chakra must be very precise -- mooladhara,
swadhisthana, manipura, anahata, vishuddhi, ajna; ajna, vishuddhi,
anahata, manipura, swadhisthana, mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Guide the consciousness through the chakras in sushumna, ascending and
descending four more times.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 9: Ending the practice]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now begin to end the practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring the awareness back to the body and chant [Om]{.class5827-0} three
times.
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice 2: Musical chakra meditation
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Sound is a particularly effective and enjoyable means of developing
awareness of the chakras. This is why nada yoga is so powerful in
spiritual awakening. The seven notes of the musical scale correspond to
the vibration of the seven chakras from mooladhara to sahasrara, and
this is the basis for a very effective musical meditation technique. The
best instrument of all is the human voice, which can be supplemented by
the harmonium. However, other instruments such as the tampura and tabla
can also be used.
:::

+---------------+---------------+---------------------------------------+

| :::           | :::           | :::                                   |

| :::           | :::           | :::                                   |
+---------------+---------------+---------------------------------------+
| ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455                         |
| Mi            | Manipura      | Ga    ![](image2490.jpg){.class2491}  |
| :::           | :::           | :::                                   |
+---------------+---------------+---------------------------------------+
| ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455                         |

| :::           | :::           | :::                                   |

| :::           | :::           | :::                                   |
+---------------+---------------+---------------------------------------+
| ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455                         |
| La            | Ajna          | Dha  ![](image2522.jpg){.class2491}   |
| :::           | :::           | :::                                   |
+---------------+---------------+---------------------------------------+
| ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455                         |
| Ti            | Bindu         | Ni    ![](image2532.jpg){.class2533}  |
| :::           | :::           | :::                                   |
+---------------+---------------+---------------------------------------+
| ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455                         |
| Do            | Sahasrara     | Sa    ![](image2543.jpg){.class2465}  |
| :::           | :::           | :::                                   |
+---------------+---------------+---------------------------------------+

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_264 .class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Technique]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 1]{.class5840-1} [: At first the musical scale of the harmonium
is ascended very slowly while the awareness begins in mooladhara and
ascends sushumna from one chakra to the next, feeling each note vibrate
in the spinal column in the region of its corresponding
chakra.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When sahasrara is attained, descend the awareness with the musical scale
down through sushumna to mooladhara. The consciousness ascends and
descends sushumna with the scale many times, slowly speeding up as
chakra location becomes quick and effortless.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 2]{.class5840-1} [: Now the voice is integrated with the notes.
The names of the chakras are chanted very precisely. The names
themselves are mantras, and if intoned with the correct note and
pronunciation, each centre can be set vibrating, and the sushumna
passage and the whole body begin to vibrate with energy. This practice
is very powerful. It can be continued for ten minutes or
more.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 3]{.class5840-1} [: In this stage the awareness still ascends and
descends through sushumna with the musical scale, but the voice makes a
continuous a-a-a-a-a-a sound (as in 'calm') as it ascends and descends
through the chakras. In the final stage, the full power of the voice is
released and a tremendous energy is generated, provided the pitch is
maintained accurately.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_265 .class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice 3: Chaturtha Pranayama (fourth pranayama)
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Chaturtha pranayama combines breathing, mantra and chakra awareness.
Although it is not widely taught, it is a powerful technique that is
both a pranayama and a meditation. This practice will lead to deeper
awareness and knowledge of the chakras. It is also a preparatory
technique for kriya yoga as it develops sensitivity to both the psychic
spinal passage and the chakras.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Chaturtha pranayama]{.class5827-1} [means 'fourth pranayama' or
'pranayama of the fourth state', or a transcendental state where words
and definitions fail to reach.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Technique]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 1: Breath awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in any comfortable meditative posture.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold the head and spine erect and close the eyes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breathe deeply.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Let the breath become deeper and more subtle.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Fix your awareness on the rhythmical flow of the breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue for a number of rounds.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 2: Mantra awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Mentally synchronize the manta [Om]{.class5827-0} with the breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The sound 'O' should synchronize with inhalation.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The sound 'm-m-m-m-m' should synchronize with exhalation. This sound
should only be mental.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breathe through the nose, keeping the mouth closed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue in this manner with awareness of the flow of the breath and the
mantra.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 3: Chakra awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now fix your attention at the eyebrow centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel you are breathing in through that centre with the mental sound 'O'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue with awareness of the breath, mantra and psychic centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Focus your attention on mooladhara.
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_266 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
With inhalation and the sound 'O-o-o-o-o', feel the breath passing up
through the spine, piercing all the chakras -- sahasrara, ajna,
vishuddhi, anahata, manipura, swadhisthana, mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue for a number of rounds.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Again fix your attention at the eyebrow centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue the mental repetition of [Om]{.class5827-0} synchronized with
the breath, but do not be aware of the breath. Only be aware of the
mantra and the psychic centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel the 'O' and the 'm-m-m-m-m' sound.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue in this manner for as long as possible.
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice 4: Chakra yoga nidra
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Yoga nidra can be used very effectively to develop your awareness of the
chakras. Here is an example of a yoga nidra/relaxation session which
includes visualization and rotation of awareness through the psychic
centres. Teachers can adopt this practice directly for their classes.
For personal use, someone can lead you through the practice, or you can
put the instructions onto a tape.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Technique]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 1: Preparation]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Place a folded blanket on the floor and lie on it in shavasana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Loosen your clothing so you feel perfectly comfortable. If necessary,
cover yourself with a blanket to keep warm, or put a sheet over you to
keep insects away.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The mouth and eyes should remain closed throughout the practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Make sure that the spinal column is straight, in line with the head and
neck, and that the hips and shoulders are fully relaxed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep the feet and legs slightly apart.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The arms should be beside your body but not touching, and the palms
should be facing up.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Adjust your position so that you feel perfectly comfortable.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Tell yourself firmly that you will not move your body throughout the
practice.
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_267 .class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 2: Sinking of the body]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Look at the space in front of your closed eyes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Imagine that the space surrounds your whole body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Your body is immersed in that space.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Simultaneously be aware of your body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It feels very light, as light as a leaf falling from a tree. Imagine
that your body is slowly sinking into the space that you see in front of
your closed eyes, like a falling leaf.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Your body is slowly sinking into the infinite space.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be aware of this feeling.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue in this manner for a few minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 3: Rhythmical breath awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of your breathing.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Awareness of the rise and fall of the navel with each breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you breathe in, feel you are sucking in air through the navel.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you breathe out, imagine that you are pushing air out from the navel.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It is a rhythmical process. Do not alter the natural breath in any way,
just become aware of it.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 4: Sankalpa]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat your sankalpa in a short positive sentence.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It should be the crystallization of your spiritual aspiration and you
should not change it.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat it with feeling, from the heart, not the lips.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat your sankalpa at least three times.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 5: Visualization -- body awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now try to visualize your own body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Imagine that you are viewing it from outside.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel that your perception is outside and your body is an object of
study.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
You may find visualization difficult -- do not worry, just do your best.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If you wish, you can imagine that there is a large mirror suspended over
your body and that your body is reflected in it.
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_268 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Look at your own reflection.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
See your whole body: feet, knees, thighs, abdomen, chest, both hands,
arms, shoulders, neck, head, mouth, nose, ears, eyes, eyebrow centre,
your whole face and your whole body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Combine rotation of awareness of each part with visualization of that
part.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue in this manner for a few minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 6: Psychic centres -- rotation of awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now you have to discover the location of the chakras.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
You must develop awareness of each psychic centre .
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Start from the base of the spine and move your awareness upward.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
First become aware of mooladhara. In the male body it is situated in the
perineum, between the anus and genitals, and in the female body it is
located at the cervix -- the mouth of the womb.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to feel the sensation at mooladhara. It is a very specific point
which you are trying to isolate.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you have found it, repeat mentally, 'Mooladhara, mooladhara,
mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now move on to the second chakra, swadhisthana. It is located at the
base of the spine, in the coccyx.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be aware of the sensation at that point and repeat mentally,
'Swadhisthana, swadhisthana, swadhisthana'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The third chakra is manipura.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It is located in the spine in line with the navel.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel this point and mentally repeat, 'Manipura, manipura, manipura".
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then become aware of anahata chakra, located in the spine, directly
behind the centre of the chest.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to locate that point exactly and mentally repeat, 'Anahata, anahata,
anahata'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now bring your awareness to vishuddhi chakra, situated in the spine,
directly behind the throat pit.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel the sensation arising at that point and mentally repeat,
'Vishuddhi, vishuddhi, vishuddhi'.
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_269 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
The next chakra is ajna.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Ajna chakra is located at the very top of the spine in the region of the
pineal gland, directly behind the eyebrow centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Fix your awareness on that area and mentally repeat, 'Ajna, ajna, ajna'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now bring your awareness to bindu, at the top back portion of the head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel that tiny point as precisely as possible, and repeat mentally,
'Bindu, bindu, bindu'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Finally, become aware of sahasrara, at the crown of the head, and repeat
mentally, 'Sahasrara, sahasrara, sahasrara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now repeat this process, slowly descending through the chakras in
reverse order: sahasrara, bindu, ajna, vishuddhi, anahata, manipura,
swadhisthana and mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is one complete round of chakra rotation.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now start a second round: mooladhara, swadhisthana, manipura, anahata,
vishuddhi, ajna, bindu, sahasrara; sahasrara, bindu, ajna, vishuddhi,
anahata, manipura, swadhisthana, mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This completes the second round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Begin a third round, this time a little faster.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you fix your attention at each point, try to feel a slight vibration
there, a tiny pulsation.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If you wish, you can chant [Om]{.class5827-0} mentally as you locate
each point in turn.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise at least five rounds and as many more as time permits.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 7: Psychic centres -- visualization]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now try to visualize the symbols of each chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
You can use your own personal system of psychic symbols or the
traditional chakra symbols as follows.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As each chakra is named, try to feel that point being lightly pressed by
the thumb, and simultaneously visualize the symbol.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The psychic symbol for mooladhara is a deep red, four-petalled lotus.
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_270 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inside there is a smoky lingam around which a snake is coiled three and
a half times. The snake's head is facing upward.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to visualize this symbol to the best of your ability and associate
it with that particular location in the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then proceed to swadhisthana chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The symbol is a six-petalled vermilion lotus, within which is depicted a
starry night above the sea. The main focal point is the crescent moon.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to visualize this symbol.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Move to manipura chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It is symbolized by a ten-petalled yellow lotus, and in the centre is
blazing fire.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Visualize this symbol, imagining that the lotus is actually growing from
manipura chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Proceed to anahata chakra, represented by a twelve-petalled blue lotus.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
In the centre is a solitary flame burning in the darkness. Try to
visualize this symbol while feeling the exact position in the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Move to vishuddhi chakra, symbolized by a sixteen-petalled purple lotus.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
In the middle there is a pure white drop of nectar.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Visualize this location in the body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then proceed to ajna chakra which is symbolized by a two-petalled
silver-grey lotus.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
On the left hand petal is the full moon and on the right hand petal, a
glowing sun.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
In the centre is a black lingam and an [Om]{.class5827-0} sign.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Create a mental image of this symbol and its exact location.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Move on to bindu. It is symbolized by a tiny white drop of nectar.
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_271 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Visualize this symbol at the top back of the head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Finally, move to sahasrara, the fountainhead of all the chakras.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It is represented by a thousand-petalled lotus. In the centre is a white
lingam.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Visualize this symbol at the crown of the head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now visualize all these symbols in the reverse order: sahasrara, bindu,
ajna, vishuddhi, anahata, manipura, swadhisthana and mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is the end of one round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Spend a few seconds visualizing each centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do a few more rounds according to the amount of time available.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 8: Eyebrow centre awareness]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Fix your attention at the eyebrow centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel your pulse at this point.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of its continuous rhythmical beat.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Mentally synchronize repetition of the mantra [Om]{.class5827-0} with
this pulse.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue for a few minutes.
:::

::: {.class1632 lang="en-us"}
[Stage 9: Sankalpa/Ending the practice]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat your sankalpa three times with full emphasis and feeling.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of your natural breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of your whole physical body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of the outer sense perceptions.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Slowly begin to move your body. When you have fully externalized your
awareness, slowly sit up and open your eyes.
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice 5: Unmani mudra (attitude of mindlessness)
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Unmani mudra is an excellent practice for developing awareness of the
chakras in the spine, from bindu down to mooladhara. It is also an
integral part of many of the kriya yoga practices (nada, pawan and
shabda sanchalana, maha mudra and maha bheda mudra), and therefore it
should be mastered before attempting to learn and practise these
techniques.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[The word]{.class-0} [unmani]{.class5827-1} [means, 'no mind' or
'thoughtlessness', and refers to the state which arises during
meditation. Therefore, unmani mudra means, 'the attitude of mindlessness
or thoughtlessness'.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_272 .class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Technique]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in any comfortable meditation pose, preferably siddhasana/siddha
yoni asana or padmasana with the back straight.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Open the eyes fully, without focusing on anything external.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Take a deep breath in and, holding the breath inside, focus the
awareness at bindu.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you breathe out, imagine the breath going down the spine.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Simultaneously, let your awareness descend the spine, passing through
all the chakras: ajna, vishuddhi, anahata, manipura, swadhisthana,
mooladhara, one after the other.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The eyes should slowly close and be fully closed by the time the
awareness reaches mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Although the eyes remain open throughout the practice, the attention
should be internalized on the chakras and breath; that is, the eyes are
open, but you are looking within. Do not try too hard, but allow the
process to occur spontaneously.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This is one round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale deeply and begin the second round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do 11 rounds.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Physically this practice is very easy
to perform. The emphasis, however, should be on the mental process
taking place. When the eyes are open they should not register anything
outside.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice 6: Beeja Mantra Sanchalana (conducting the seed sound)
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
This practice is one of the techniques of kriya yoga, but is not
normally one of the twenty kriyas that we teach. It is concerned with
mentally repeating the beeja mantra of each kshetram and chakra, one
after the other, whilst simultaneously moving the awareness through each
chakra.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[The word]{.class-0} [beeja]{.class5827-1} [means 'seed', mantra means
'mystic sound' and sanchalana means 'conduction'. Therefore, this
practice can be called 'the conduction of the seed sound'.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_273 .class185 lang="en-us"}
Psychic passages
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
In the following kriya, beeja mantra sanchalana, as well as in a number
of practices of kriya yoga, you will be required tomove your awareness
through two psychic passages called [arohan]{.class5827-0} and
[awarohan.]{.class5827-0} The path of these passages is as follows:
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Arohan]{.class5827-1} [, the ascending passage, goes from mooladhara
chakra, forward to swadhisthana kshetram in the pubic area, then follows
the curve of the belly to manipura kshetram, upward to anahata kshetram
and vishuddhi kshetram in the front of the throat, then in a straight
line to bindu at the top back of the head.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[There is also another pathway for the arohan psychic passage that has
been taught by tradition throughout the ages. On the ascent from
mooladhara, swadhisthana kshetram and onwards, the awareness is taken
from vishuddhi kshetram to lalana chakra in the palate, then to the
nosetip, to the eyebrow centre, and following the curvature of the skull
through sahasrara at the top of the head, to bindu at the back of the
crown, where there is a little whorl of hair. In this book we will refer
to the arohan passage as connecting vishuddhi kshetram directly to
bindu; however, you can experiment with both passages and use whichever
one suits you best.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Awarohan]{.class5827-1} [is the descending passage which starts at
bindu, travels forward to ajna chakra, then down through sushumna in the
spine, passing through all the chakras in turn to finally terminate at
mooladhara.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[In the following practice you will have to familiarize yourself with
these two psychic passages, and this will also be useful as a
preparation for the kundalini kriyas.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Beeja mantras
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
The beeja mantras for each kshetram and chakra are as follows:
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[1. Mooladhara --]{.class-1} [Lam]{.class5827-2}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[2. Swadhisthana --]{.class-1} [Vam]{.class5827-2}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[3. Manipura --]{.class-1} [Ram]{.class5827-2}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[4. Anahata --]{.class-1} [Yam]{.class5827-2}
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_274 .class2016 lang="en-us"}
[5. Vishuddhi --]{.class-1} [Ham]{.class5827-2}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[6. Ajna --]{.class-1} [Om]{.class5827-2}
:::

::: {.class2016 lang="en-us"}
[7. Bindu --]{.class-1} [Om]{.class5827-2}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[Technique]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in any comfortable position, preferably siddhasana/siddha yoni
asana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep the head and spine straight and the eyes closed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Throughout the practice there is no physical movement; the kriya is
performed mentally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring your attention to mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat the mantra [Lam]{.class5827-0} mentally, once, and try to feel
the vibration at mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then ascend through arohan.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Let your attention jump to swadhisthana kshetram and repeat the mantra
[Vam]{.class5827-0} , feeling the vibration at that point.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Jump to manipura kshetram and repeat the mantra [Ram.]{.class5827-0}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At anahata kshetram, [Yam]{.class5827-0} .
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At vishuddhi kshetram, [Ham.]{.class5827-0}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At bindu, [Om]{.class5827-0} .
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then descend through awarohan.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat [Om]{.class5827-0} at ajna, in the centre of the head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat [Ham]{.class5827-0} at vishuddhi chakra in the spine.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At anahata chakra, [Yam.]{.class5827-0}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At manipura chakra, [Ram]{.class5827-0} .
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At swadhisthana, [Vam]{.class5827-0} .
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then return to the starting point, mooladhara, and begin the next round
by repeating the mantra [Lam]{.class5827-0} .
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Your awareness should jump from one centre to the next.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do 9 rounds, or more if you have time.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Beeja mantra sanchalana is an excellent
preparatory practice for kriya yoga sadhana. You may also practise this
by spending some time, for example five minutes, at each kshetram or
chakra, chanting the mantra out loud on a low key and feeling it
vibrating at the chakra.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {#part0047.xhtml_page_275 .class185 lang="en-us"}
Practice 7: Drawing the chakras
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Drawing of mandalas, such as the chakras, is an important part of
tantra. Many of the practices require that the correct mandalas be
constructed first of all. The creation of a chakra diagram should be
done with absolute awareness and concentration, and its measurements and
dimensions must be exact. You should try to ensure that you will be
undisturbed for at least an hour, and approach the exercise as you do
meditation. In some Tibetan Buddhist monasteries, mandalas are drawn and
painted as part of the daily sadhana, as is the practice in several
Greek Orthodox monasteries, where icons are painted in minute detail as
daily meditation.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Make sure you have all the necessary materials; pencils, pens, rubbers,
ruler, compass, colours or paints, so that you will not have to disturb
your concentration once you have started. If you have a sadhana room,
then that is the best place to create your mandalas. A good size for
drawing the chakras on art paper is about 9" square, as this size is
most useful for visual display and concentration practices. Larger and
smaller sized chakras can be made for other purposes.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[By first using only a black pen, one can plainly see the simple yet
subtle lines and formations, and discover the hidden symbology as it
becomes visually clearer in the mind. The next step is to colour it,
according to the traditional colours described in the text. In this way,
mandalas of each of the seven chakras can be completed over seven or
more sessions.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[This practice is very relaxing and enjoyable. You may like to create
more subjective and artistic impressions of the chakras, with your own
colours and symbols, as you come to understand them in a personal way.
This expands your awareness to the many possibilities of experiencing
not only the chakras, but life itself.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[The chakras should not be interpreted on just one or two levels, but in
many dimensions. After drawing and painting the chakras successfully,
you can then take the next step and create the chakras in a three
dimensional form. For this you]{.class-0} []{#part0047.xhtml_page_276
.class-0} [can use any number of materials such as clay, plasticine,
wire, fibreglass, copper or stone.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class202 lang="en-us"}
[You must remember, however, that the traditional drawings are as
subjective as your feelings and experiences of the chakra. Therefore,
use your own experiences to express the deeper and inner spiritual
aspects, on paper, in clay or stone, etc. Through this, you will find a
clarity of vision arising out of what once seemed a confused and blurred
picture of life.]{.class-0}
:::

[]{#part0048.xhtml}

::: {#part0048.xhtml_page_277 .class216 lang="en-us"}

:::

::: {.class2767 lang="en-us"}
The practices of kundalini yoga must be adopted systematically. We
suggest that you practise and perfect the sadhana for each chakra for
one month or more, before moving on to the next. The sadhana will
continue for eight months, as outlined below:

[]{#part0049.xhtml}

::: {#part0049.xhtml_page_279 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[37](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5974)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Kundalini Kriyas\
of Kriya Yoga](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5974)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[T]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} he following tantric kriyas provide what is
possibly the most efficient method for systematically evolving man's
consciousness that has ever been developed. They are said to have been
the teachings for the transcendental sadhana which Lord Shiva gave to
his disciple and wife, Parvati.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[By tradition, kriya yoga was never taught publicly. The kriyas were
always communicated verbally from guru to disciple. It is only in recent
years that these kriyas have been published in accordance with the needs
of this era.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[These kriyas are rather advanced and too powerful for the average
aspirant. Before an aspirant takes up their practice, he or she should
have a thorough familiarity with and practical experience of all the
preliminary practices included in the book. Also, it is advisable that
he takes up these kriyas only under the guidance of a guru, who can see
that the aspirant is fully prepared for them and that any obstacles
which arise while the aspirant is practising do not cause any harm in
the way of disease, mental imbalance or psychic dislocation.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[If possible, try to come to an ashram for one month for full initiation
into the higher practices of kriya yoga.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Preparation
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
One must realize that all the rules and regulations which were
enumerated at the beginning of this practice section
[]{#part0049.xhtml_page_280} also apply to all the aspirants who wish to
successfully learn and practise kriya yoga.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[It is essential that one has developed sensitivity to the positions of
the chakras and kshetram by practising the techniques given for the
individual chakras (]{.class-0} [[chapters
28]{.class-0}](#part0040.xhtml){.class5828-4} [to]{.class-0}
[[34]{.class-0}](#part0046.xhtml){.class5828-4} [), and also the
techniques for integrated chakra awareness (]{.class-0} [[chapter
35]{.class-0}](#part0047.xhtml){.class5828-4} [). This sensitivity
should be such that you can feel them both physically and
mentally.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[You should also know the position of the two psychic pathways known
as]{.class-0} [arohan]{.class5827-1} [and]{.class-0}
[awarohan]{.class5827-1} [. They are explained in the practice called
'Beeja mantra sanchalana' in]{.class-0} [[chapter
35]{.class-0}](#part0047.xhtml){.class5828-4} [. The following
techniques are integral parts of the 20 kriyas:]{.class-0}
:::

+------------------------------+---------------+
| ::: class2983                | ::: class2983 |
| Name                         | Chapter       |
| :::                          | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Vipareeta karani asana       | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 33            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Ujjayi pranayama             | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 33            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Siddhasana/Siddha yoni asana | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 26            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Unmani mudra                 | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 35            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Khechari mudra               | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 33            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Ajapa japa                   | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 32            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Utthanpadasana               | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 26            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Shambhavi mudra              | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 28            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Moola bandha                 | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 29            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Nasikagra drishti            | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 29            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Uddiyana bandha              | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 31            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Jalandhara bandha            | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 33            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Bhadrasana                   | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 26            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Padmasana                    | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 26            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Shanmukhi mudra              | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 34            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+
| Vajroli/Sahajoli mudra       | ::: class2446 |
|                              | 30            |
|                              | :::           |
+------------------------------+---------------+

::: {.class306 lang="en-us"}
[These practices are all fully described in the chapters indicated and
it is essential that you master them. If you try to learn kriya yoga
without first of all perfecting them, then you will find the actual
kriya techniques very difficult to follow and you will get very little
benefit from them.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {#part0049.xhtml_page_281 .class185 lang="en-us"}
Mode of learning the kriyas
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
It is not possible to learn all the kriyas at once. Therefore, we
suggest that you learn each kriya sequentially, spending at least one
week mastering each kriya, and progressively adding each new kriya to
those already learned. That is, in the first week learn and master kriya
1: vipareeta karani mudra. Then in the second week, learn kriya 2:
chakra anusandhana, and do both 1 and 2 daily. In the third week, learn
kriya 3: nada sanchalana and do it daily, together with the previous two
kriyas. In this way, all the kriyas can be systematically and thoroughly
learned in a period of 20 weeks. However, it may take many months of
regular practice before the kriyas are perfected and remember kundalini
kriyas should be practised under guidance.
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Length of practice
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
As you progressively add more and more kriyas to your practice program,
the time required for daily practice will increase. Eventually, after
mastering all the kriyas, your daily practice of the 20 kriyas, with the
required number of rounds, will take between two and two and a half
hours.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[If you can spare this amount of time every day, then you will get the
maximum benefit. However, most people, no matter how sincere, will not
be able to devote this length of time to their practice. Therefore, for
those who wish to practise kriya yoga, but have less spare time, we
suggest that you reduce the number of rounds per kriya as
follows:]{.class-0}
:::

+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2983                             |   | ::: class2983      |   | ::: class2983      |
| Kriya technique                           |   | Full               |   | Reduced            |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 1: Vipareeta karani mudra                 |   | 21                 |   | 11                 |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 2: Chakra anusandhana                     |   | 9                  |   | 9                  |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 3: Nada sanchalana                        |   | 13                 |   | 5                  |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 4: Pawan sanchalana                       |   | 49                 |   | 11                 |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 5: Shabda sanchalana                      |   | 59                 |   | 11                 |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 6: Maha mudra                             |   | 12                 |   | 6                  |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 7: Maha bheda mudra                       |   | 12                 |   | 6                  |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 8: Manduki kriya                          |   | 1--3 mins          |   | 1--3 mins          |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: {#part0049.xhtml_page_282 .class2455} |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 9: Tadan kriya                            |   | 7                  |   | 7                  |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 10: Naumukhi mudra                        |   | 5                  |   | 5                  |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 11: Shakti chalini                        |   | 5                  |   | 5                  |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 12: Shambhavi                             |   | 11                 |   | 5                  |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 13: Amrit pan                             |   | 9                  |   | 9                  |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 14: Chakra bhedan                         |   | 59                 |   | 11                 |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 15: Sushumna darshan                      |   | --                 |   | --                 |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 16: Prana ahuti                           |   | 1 min              |   | 1 min              |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 17: Utthan                                |   | 2--3 mins          |   | 2--3 mins          |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 18: Swaroopa darshan                      |   | 2--3 mins          |   | 2--3 mins          |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 19: Linga sanchalana                      |   | 2--3 mins          |   | 2--3 mins          |
