| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+
| ::: class2455                             |   | ::: class2446      |   | ::: class2446      |
| 20: Dhyana                                |   | --                 |   | --                 |
| :::                                       |   | :::                |   | :::                |
+-------------------------------------------+---+--------------------+---+--------------------+

::: {.class306 lang="en-us"}
[This daily program containing all the kriyas, with a reduced number of
rounds, will take a total of about one to one and a half hours. The
benefits may be slightly less than when you do the complete number of
rounds per kriya, but still you will reap much fruit from your
practise.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[While learning each kriya, you should do the full number of rounds;
this can be reduced as you integrate the next kriya.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Hints on practice
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
The following suggestions will help you to master the kriyas and gain
maximum benefit:
:::

::: {.class793 lang="en-us"}
[1. Do not strain physically or mentally under any circumstances, or you
may experience negative side effects. This applies particularly in the
case of kriyas such as maha mudra, maha bheda mudra, tadan kriya,
naumukhi and shakti chalini. Regular daily practice will gradually bring
such changes into the mind and body, so that after some time, you will
be able to practise the kriyas almost effortlessly.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class793 lang="en-us"}
[2. Do not hold your breath for longer than is comfortable. In many of
the kriyas, such as maha mudra and maha bheda mudra, most people will
initially find difficulty in completing a full round in one respiration
cycle]{.class-1} []{#part0049.xhtml_page_283 .class-1} [without strain
or suffocation. In the beginning, it may be necessary to break in the
middle of each round, or to take a short rest at the end of each round
and take a few normal breaths. As you develop the capacity to hold the
breath for longer periods, and to control inhalation and exhalation,
this concession may be disregarded.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class793 lang="en-us"}
[3. After long inner breath retentions, it is best to breathe in
slightly before breathing out. In many of the kriyas, such as maha
mudra, maha bheda mudra, naumukhi and shakti chalini, where the breath
is held inside for prolonged periods, there is a tendency for the lungs
to lock. The best way to overcome this problem and release the lungs is
to breathe in slightly before breathing out. This will make the kriyas
much easier to do.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class3266 lang="en-us"}
[4. While learning each kriya, check that you are doing all the steps
and that they are being done correctly.]{.class-1}
:::

[]{#part0050.xhtml}

::: {#part0050.xhtml_page_284 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[38](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5959)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[The Kriya Yoga Practices](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5959)
:::

::: {.class2767 lang="en-us"}
By tradition there are a total of 76 kundalini kriyas of kriya yoga. We
present the following 20 main practices, which are sufficient for the
daily practice of any sincere sadhaka.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[These practices are divided into three groups:]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class793 lang="en-us"}
[1. those which induce pratyahara]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class793 lang="en-us"}
[2. those which induce dharana]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class793 lang="en-us"}
[3. those which induce dhyana]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
It should be noted that these three states are actually a continuity of
evolution, that is, the consciousness flows from one to the next without
any apparent dividing point -- so these practices should be done in an
unbroken sequence. Of course, from the first day, the practice of these
kriyas will not necessarily lead to such exalted states of awareness,
but if they are practised properly with correct guidance, by an aspirant
who is ready for them, then most likely, one day they will. It will be
at that stage that the constant, unbroken progression of awareness will
become essential. Remember, you should learn one kriya per week.
:::

[]{#part0051.xhtml}

::: {#part0051.xhtml_page_285 .class3286 lang="en-us"}
PRATYAHARA PRACTICES
:::

::: class3290-1
![](image3289.jpg){.class3290-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[1: Vipareeta Karani Mudra (the attitude of inversion)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Assume vipareeta karani asana (described in [chapter
33](#part0045.xhtml) ).
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The chin should not touch the chest.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise subtle ujjayi pranayama Be sure that the legs are completely
vertical. Close the eyes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale with ujjayi and simultaneously feel a hot stream of amrit or
nectar flowing through the spinal passage from manipura chakra to
vishuddhi in the throat. The nectar will collect at vishuddhi.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Retain the breath for a few seconds, and be aware of the nectar
remaining at vishuddhi and becoming cool.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then exhale with ujjayi, sensing the nectar travelling from vishuddhi
through ajna, bindu and to sahasrara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The sensation is that of the nectar being injected with the help of the
breath.
:::

::: {#part0051.xhtml_page_286 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
After exhalation, immediately return your awareness to manipura and
repeat the kriya to bring more nectar down to vishuddhi, and finally to
sahasrara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise 21 respirations or rounds.
:::

::: class3304-0
![](image3303.jpg){.class3304-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[2: Chakra Anusandhana (discovery of the chakras)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Assume siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The eyes remain closed throughout the practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breathe normally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
There is no connection between the breath and the consciousness in this
practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring your awareness to mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Your consciousness will slowly ascend the frontal passage of arohan from
mooladhara to the frontal point of swadhisthana at the pubic bone,
manipura at the navel, anahata at the sternum, the chest centre,
vishuddhi at the throat and across to bindu at the top, back of the
head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you travel upward, mentally repeat, 'mooladhara, swadhisthana,
manipura, anahata, vishuddhi, bindu', as you pass through these centres.
:::

::: {#part0051.xhtml_page_287 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then let your awareness slip down the spinal awarohan passage from bindu
to mooladhara, mentally repeating 'ajna, vishuddhi, anahata, manipura,
swadhisthana, mooladhara' as you pass through these centres.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
From mooladhara, immediately start ascending in the frontal passage as
before, mentally reciting the chakra names as you ascend, starting with
swadhisthana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue this rotation of awareness through the chakras in a constant
flow of rounds.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not make a serious, tense effort to locate the chakras as you pass
through them. Merely glance at them as you go by, as you would view the
scenery from a fast moving train.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If you wish, you can visualize your awareness in this kriya as a thin
silver serpent travelling in an ellipse within your body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise 9 rounds.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[3: Nada Sanchalana (conducting the sound consciousness)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Exhale completely.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Open the eyes and bend the head forward, so that it drops downward in a
relaxed manner. The chin should not press tightly on the chest.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring the awareness to mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then, as you inhale, your consciousness should rise up through the
frontal passage of arohan to bindu.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Have a clear awareness of swadhisthana, manipura, anahata and vishuddhi,
as you pass through them on your way to bindu, and mentally repeat their
names.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As your awareness travels from vishuddhi to bindu during the last
segment of your inhalation, your head will slowly rise and tilt back
slightly into position facing about 20 degrees above the horizontal.
With the breath retainedinside and the awareness at bindu, mentally
repeat, 'bindu, bindu, bindu'.
:::

::: class3331-1
![](image3330.jpg){#page_288 .class3331-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1642 lang="en-us"}
The power of the awareness will build up as you are repeating the word
'bindu' and it will explode into the vocal chant of [Om]{.class5827-0} ,
which will carry you down through the spinal passage of awarohan to
mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The 'O' sound will explode and move downwards, culminating almost in a
vibrating m-m-m sound as you approach mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As your awareness descends in the spine, your eyes will gradually close
into unmani mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you descend through the awarohan passage with the [Om]{.class5827-0}
sound, you should also be aware of ajna, vishuddhi, anahata, manipura
and swadhisthana chakras; no mental repetition. When you have reached
mooladhara, open the eyes and drop the head forward.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Mentally repeat, 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara', with the breath
retained outside and start on the ascent as before, with inhalation and
repetition of the chakra names as you pass through them.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise 13 full rounds or breaths and end after the last 'mooladhara,
mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: class3341-1
![](image3340.jpg){#page_289 .class3341-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[4: Pawan Sanchalana (conducting the breath consciousness)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in padmasana, siddhasana or siddha yoni asana, with the eyes closed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise khechari mudra and ujjayi pranayama throughout this kriya.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Exhale completely, open the eyes and bend the head forward as in nada
sanchalana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of mooladhara chakra and repeat mentally, 'mooladhara,
mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then mentally say 'arohan' once and begin your ascent through the
frontal passage with a subtle ujjayi inhalation.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you ascend, be aware of the chakras and as you pass name them
mentally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As your awareness moves from vishuddhi to bindu, slowly raise your head
until it leans backward as in nada sanchalana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At bindu mentally repeat, 'bindu, bindu, bindu'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then say 'awarohan' mentally and descend through the spinal passage with
ujjayi exhalation, mentally repeating the name of each chakra as you
pass through it.
:::

::: {#part0051.xhtml_page_290 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you descend, your eyes will close very gradually into unmani mudra,
the attitude of drowsiness.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At mooladhara they will be closed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then open your eyes and bend your head forward.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Again begin your ascent with ujjayi inhalation, as before.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise 49 rounds or complete breaths.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After the last 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara', open your eyes and
end the practice.
:::

::: class3362-1
![](image3361.jpg){.class3362-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[5: Shabda Sanchalana (conducting the word consciousness)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana. Practise khechari
mudra and ujjayi pranayama throughout the kriya.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Exhale completely, open the eyes, bend the head forward and become aware
of mooladhara chakra for a few seconds. Inhale with ujjayi and ascend
the frontal passage.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you ascend, be aware of the sound of the breath which takes the form
of the mantra [So]{.class5827-0} .
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Simultaneously, be aware of each kshetram, without mental repetition.
:::

::: {#part0051.xhtml_page_291 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you travel from vishuddhi to bindu, the head will move upward as in
pawan sanchalana and nada sanchalana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then, with the breath retained inside, be aware of bindu for a few
seconds.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then descend the spinal passage performing unmani mudra and being
simultaneously aware of the natural sound of exhalation and the mantra
[Ham]{.class5827-0} .
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be aware of each chakra without repetition of its name.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After reaching mooladhara, open the eyes and lower your head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Begin your ujjayi inhalation, rising through the frontal passage with
the inhalation mantra of [So]{.class5827-0} .
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Continue in this manner for 59 full rounds or breaths.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[6: Maha Mudra (great attitude)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana or siddha yoni asana, with the heel of the lower foot
pressing firmly in towards mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise khechari mudra, exhale completely and bend the head forward.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep the eyes open in the beginning.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Ascend through the frontal passage with ujjayi inhalation, being aware
of each kshetram as you pass through it.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Raise your head as you are crossing from vishuddhi to bindu.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At bindu repeat mentally, 'bindu, bindu, bindu'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise moola bandha and shambhavi mudra with the breath still retained
inside.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Say to yourself mentally, 'shambhavi-khechari-mool', while shifting your
awareness to the centre of these practices.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you say 'shambhavi', your awareness should be fixed at the eyebrow
centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you say 'khechari', your awareness should be fixed at the tongue
and roof of the mouth.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you say 'mool', your awareness should be fixed at mooladhara
chakra.
:::

::: class3391-1
![](image3390.jpg){#page_292 .class3391-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {#part0051.xhtml_page_293 .class1642 lang="en-us"}
Beginners should repeat this shifting of awareness 3 times.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Advanced aspirants can rotate their awareness up to 12 times.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then, first release shambhavi mudra, then moola bandha.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring your awareness back to bindu and travel down your spinal passage
to mooladhara, with ujjayi exhalation and unmani mudra, and be aware of
the chakras as you pass through them.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
On reaching mooladhara, bend the head forward and open the eyes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then repeat, 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara' and ascend the frontal
passage with ujjayi inhalation, as before.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise 12 full rounds or breaths and end after the last 'mooladhara,
mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Alternative practice]{.class5840-1} [: This kriya can also be practised
in utthanpadasana.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When practising maha mudra in utthanpadasana, a slight change must be
made in the technique.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After ascending to bindu, repeat 'bindu, bindu, bindu'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Lean forward and hold the big toe of the extended foot with the fingers
of both hands, to form utthanpadasana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The stretched knee must not bend.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now practise moola bandha and shambhavi mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat, 'shambhavi-khechari-mool' from 3 to 12 times, passing your
awareness to the locations of these practices as you repeat their names.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Release shambhavi, then moola bandha, then utthanpadasana. Sit upright
and place the hands back on theknee. Bring your awareness back to bindu,
and then descend the spinal passage with ujjayi exhalation and unmani
mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise 4 rounds with the right leg stretched forward, 4 rounds with
the left leg stretched forward, and 4 rounds with both legs stretched
forward.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note:]{.class5829-0} [This kriya can either be practised in
perfect siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or in utthanpadasana. Both
alternatives are equally good, as both apply a firm and constant
pressure at mooladhara. If you can easily sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni
asana, then the best method is the first one described. If you cannot
sit comfortably in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana, then use the
alternative. It is easy to become sleepy while doing kriya yoga and this
alternative has an added advantage of helping to remove
sleepiness.]{.class-4}
:::

::: class3412-0
![](image3411.jpg){#page_294 .class3412-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {#part0051.xhtml_page_295 .class1642 lang="en-us"}
The names of the chakras and kshetram can also be repeated mentally as
you ascend and descend arohan and awarohan.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[7: Maha Bheda Mudra (great piercing attitude)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana or siddha yoni asana, with the heel of the lower foot
pressing firmly in towards mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise khechari mudra and exhale completely, with the eyes open. Bend
the head forward.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale with ujjayi and ascend the frontal passage to bindu.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you ascend from vishuddhi to bindu, raise your head.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'bindu, bindu, bindu', and then descend the spinal
passage to mooladhara with ujjayi exhalation and unmani mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be sure to notice the chakras as you pass through them. Then practise
jalandhara bandha with the breath retained outside. Practise nasikagra
drishti, uddiyana bandha and moola bandha.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'nasikagra-uddiyana-mool', while simultaneously placing
your awareness at the seats of these practices in turn.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat this cycle of awareness 3 times if you are a beginner, or up to
12 times if you are experienced.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then release nasikagra drishti, moola bandha, uddiyana bandha and
jalandhara bandha, but keep the head down.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring your awareness back to mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat the mantra 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara', mentally.
:::

::: class3430-0
![](image3429.jpg){#page_296 .class3430-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1642 lang="en-us"}
Then with ujjayi inhalation, ascend the frontal passage to bindu for the
next round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise 12 full rounds or breaths.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Alternative practice]{.class5840-1} [: This kriya can also be practised
in utthanpadasana, as with maha mudra.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Place the hands on the bent knee, exhale completely and bend the head
forward, keeping the eyes open.
:::

::: {#part0051.xhtml_page_297 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale with ujjayi through the frontal passage from mooladhara to bindu,
raising your head while moving from vishuddhi to bindu.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat, 'bindu, bindu, bindu', and then exhale with ujjayi down the
spinal passage, doing unmani mudra and being aware of each chakra en
route.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold the breath outside and bend forward to grasp the big toe of the
extended foot to form utthanpadasana. Press the chin against the chest
to form jalandhara bandha.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise nasikagra drishti, uddiyana bandha and moola bandha, while
still retaining the breath outside.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'nasikagra-uddiyana-mool', while placing the awareness
at the locations of these practices in turn.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat this cycle of awareness 3 times if you are a beginner, or up to
12 times if you are experienced.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Release nasikagra drishti, moola bandha and uddiyana bandha.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring your hands to your knees and sit up straight. Release jalandhara
but keep your head bent down.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring your awareness back to mooladhara. Repeat the mantra 'mooladhara,
mooladhara, mooladhara', and then ascend the frontal passage with ujjayi
inhalation.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise in this way for 4 full rounds or breaths with the right leg
extended, then practise 4 times with the left leg extended, and finally
4 times with both legs extended.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After the fourth time in each position, ascend once to bindu with ujjayi
inhalation. Repeat the bindu mantra, descend to mooladhara and repeat
its mantra, relax, then change legs.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The rotation of awareness through nasikagra, uddiyana and mool is done
with outside retention of the breath at mooladhara. You are advised to
practise only 3 rotations at first, slowly increasing by one rotation
per week until you can complete 12 rotations.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Make sure that all the bandhas are
performed correctly and in the right sequence. At first you will have to
pay special attention to this, but with regular practice the bandhas
will lock and tighten automatically, without effort and at the right
stage of the kriya.]{.class-4}
:::

::: class3452-0
![](image3451.jpg){#page_298 .class3452-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {#part0051.xhtml_page_299 .class1642 lang="en-us"}
Nose tip gazing helps to tighten the lock of the bandhas. Make sure that
nasikagra drishti and the bandhas are practised simultaneously and that
you do not omit any of them while rotating awareness through the
centres. Do not strain. If you are feeling pain or discomfort in the
eyes, stop nasikagra drishti but continue the bandhas and rotation of
awareness. Slowly increase duration of nasikagra as the eye muscles
adapt to the practice.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
You can repeat the 'mooladhara' mantra 3 times before applying the
bandhas as well as repeating 'mooladhara' 3 times at the beginning of a
new round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The names of the chakras and kshetrams can be mentally repeated as you
ascend and descend arohan and awarohan passages.
:::

::: class3459-1
![](image3458.jpg){.class3459-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[8: Manduki Mudra (frog attitude)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in bhadrasana. The eyes should remain open. The area of the body
below mooladhara chakra must touch the floor. If necessary place a
cushion under the buttocks to apply firm pressure to this point.
:::

::: {#part0051.xhtml_page_300 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Place the hands on the knees and practise nasikagra drishti.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of the natural breath flowing in and out of the nostrils.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
With inhalation, the breath flows through both nostrils and merges at
the eyebrow centre. As you exhale, the two flows diverge from the
eyebrow centre and move out through both nostrils.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The breath follows a conical or inverted V-shaped pathway.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel this.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Simultaneously, be aware of all smells.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The point of this kriya is to smell the aroma of the astral body which
has a scent like that of sandalwood. If your eyes become tired, close
them for a while and then resume nasikagra drishti.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise this kriya until it becomes intoxicating.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not carry it so far that you become totally absorbed in it and do not
wish to end the practice.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[9: Tadan Kriya (beating the kundalini)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in padmasana with the eyes open.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Place the palms on the floor at the sides of the body, next to the hips,
with the fingers pointing forward.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Tilt the head slightly backward and practise shambhavi mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale through the mouth in audible ujjayi pranayama.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you inhale, feel the breath travelling downward through a tube
connecting the mouth to mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The breath will collect at mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold the breath in, keep your awareness at mooladhara and practise moola
bandha.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Using your hands, lift your body off the ground.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then drop your body lightly so that mooladhara is gently beaten. Repeat
this beating 3 times.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Do not practise this quickly or harshly.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After the third beating, exhale gently through the nose with ujjayi
pranayama.
:::

::: class3486-0
![](image3485.jpg){#page_301 .class3486-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1642 lang="en-us"}
The breath will seem to diffuse in all direction from its storehouse at
mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise this kriya a total of 7 times.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The number of beatings practised per round can be gradually increased
from 3 to a maximum of 11.
:::

[]{#part0052.xhtml}

::: {#part0052.xhtml_page_302 .class3286 lang="en-us"}
DHARANA PRACTICES
:::

::: class3499-1
![](image3498.jpg){.class3499-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[10: Naumukhi Mudra (closing the nine gates)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana. The eyes should remain
closed throughout. If necessary, use a cushion to ensure mooladhara is
compressed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Perform khechari mudra and bend the head slightly forward (not
jalandhara bandha).
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then inhale with ujjayi up the frontal passage to bindu. Raise your head
as you pass from vishuddhi to bindu. Practise shanmukhi mudra by closing
your ears with the thumbs, the eyes with both forefingers, the nostrils
with your middle fingers, the upper lip with the ring fingers
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
and your lower lip with the small fingers (do not apply too much
pressure).
:::

::: class3509-1
![](image3508.jpg){#page_303 .class3509-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1642 lang="en-us"}
Practise moola bandha and vajroli/sahajoli mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The nine gates of the body are now closed (eyes, ears, nostrils, mouth,
anus and sexual organ).
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of the spinal passage and bindu.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now visualize a shining copper trident (trishul), rooted in mooladhara
with its stem in the spinal cord and the prongs extending upward from
vishuddhi. The prongs are very sharp.
:::

::: {#part0052.xhtml_page_304 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
The trishul will slightly rise a number of times of its own accord and
it will pierce bindu with its central prong.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As it pierces bindu, repeat the mantra 'bindu bhedan', which means
'bindu piercing'.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After some time, release vajroli/sahajoli mudra and moola bandha. Open
the upper gates and bring your hands down to your knees.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Exhale with ujjayi down the spinal passage from bindu to mooladhara.
Mentally repeat 'mooladhara' 3 times. Then inhale up the frontal passage
to bindu to repeat the kriya.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise 5 full rounds or breaths, and after the fifth round, end the
practice after exhalation.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: It is extremely important that the back
be held perfectly straight throughout this kriya. If not, the sensation
that follows the piercing of bindu may not be perceived.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When vajroli/sahajoli mudra is correctly performed it will also heighten
the sensation experienced during this practice. When vajroli/sahajoli
mudra is perfected, the contraction of vajra nadi can be achieved
without contracting the anal sphincter muscles. The sensation can be
compared to an electric current running the full length of vajra nadi to
the brain. Try to sensitize your awareness to the point where you
actually feel the piercing of bindu like an electric shock.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you ascend and descend arohan and awarohan, you can mentally repeat
the names of the chakras and kshetram if you wish.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[11: Shakti Chalini (conduction of the thought force)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The eyes should remain closed throughout.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise khechari mudra. Exhale completely, bend the head forward and
bring the awareness to mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Repeat mentally, 'mooladhara, mooladhara, mooladhara', and then ascend
the frontal passage to bindu with ujjayi inhalation, raising your head
as you approach bindu.
:::

::: class3530-1
![](image3529.jpg){#page_305 .class3530-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {#part0052.xhtml_page_306 .class1642 lang="en-us"}
Retain the breath inside, and then practise shanmukhi mudra, closing the
ears, eyes, nostrils and lips with the fingers. Allow your awareness to
rotate in a continuous cycle, descending the spinal passage to
mooladhara and rising up the frontal passage to bindu in an unbroken
loop, while you keep the breath retained inside.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Visualize a thin green snake moving through the psychic passageways.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The tail of this serpent is at bindu, and the body extends down through
mooladhara and up the frontal passage.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The head is also at bindu, with the mouth biting the end of the tail.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If you watch this snake, it will start to move in a circle in the
psychic passages, or it may even go off this track and follow a new one
of its own.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Just watch this snake, whatever it does.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When your retention of breath is becoming exhausted, release shanmukhi
mudra, return the hands to the knees and bring your awareness to bindu.
Then descend to mooladhara through the spinal passage with ujjayi
exhalation. At mooladhara, lower your head, repeat 'mooladhara' 3 times,
and ascend the frontal passage.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise this kriya 5 times without a break, or for the duration of 5
breaths.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: Vajroli/sahajoli mudra and moola bandha
can also be performed simultaneously with yoni mudra.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[12: Shambhavi (Parvati's lotus)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close your eyes and practise khechari mudra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Visualize a lotus flower with a long thin stem extending downward. The
roots of the lotus are white or transparent green. They spread out from
mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The thin green lotus stem is in your spinal passage.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The lotus flower is at sahasrara, and it is closed like a bud.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At the bottom of the bud are a few light green immature petals.
:::

::: class3550-1
![](image3549.jpg){#page_307 .class3550-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1642 lang="en-us"}
The main petals of the flower are pink with fine red veins.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to see this lotus clearly. You visualize it in chidakasha, but you
feel it in your body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Exhale and take your awareness to the root of the lotus at mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale with ujjayi pranayama and allow your awareness to rise slowly
through the centre of the lotus stem, within the spinal passage.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At the end of inhalation, you will reach the closed bud at the top of
the stem.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Your ascent will be like that of a caterpillar, climbing up inside a
thin stem.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Hold your awareness at sahasrara with the breath retained inside. You
are inside the lotus, but you can also see it from outside.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It will begin to open very slowly.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As the bud opens out into a beautiful lotus flower, you will see the
yellow pollen-tipped stamens in its centre.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It will slowly close again, to open again almost immediately.
:::

::: {#part0052.xhtml_page_308 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
After the lotus has stopped opening and closing, and it remains sealed,
then slowly descend through the stem to mooladhara, drifting down on the
wave of your ujjayi exhalation. Remain at mooladhara for a few seconds,
visualizing the roots spreading out in all directions.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then once again, ascend the stem with ujjayi inhalation. Ascend and
descend 11 times, and then end this kriya.
:::

::: class3566-0
![](image3565.jpg){.class3566-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[13: Amrit Pan (the quaffing of nectar)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep the eyes closed throughout and practise khechari mudra. Bring your
awareness to manipura chakra, where there is a storehouse of a warm,
sweet liquid.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Exhale fully with ujjayi. Inhale with ujjayi, drawing a quantity of this
liquid up to vishuddhi chakra through the spinal passage with the
suction power of your breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Remain at vishuddhi for a few seconds.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The nectar that you have raised from manipura will become icy cold at
vishuddhi.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then with ujjayi, exhale up to lalana chakra (at the back of the soft
palate), through the nectar passage. Blow the
[]{#part0052.xhtml_page_309} cool nectar up to lalana with the breath.
The breath will immediately disperse by itself once you have reached
lalana. Immediately return your awareness to manipura chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
With another ujjayi inhalation, continue the upward transfer of liquid.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise 9 times in all.
:::

::: class3579-0
![](image3578.jpg){.class3579-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[14: Chakra Bhedan (piercing the chakras)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana. Keep your eyes closed
throughout.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Practise khechari mudra and ujjayi pranayama.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Breathe without any break between inhalation and exhalation.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Exhale, and bring your awareness down to swadhisthana chakra at the base
of the spine.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Inhale and direct your consciousness first to mooladhara and then up the
frontal passage.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At about the level of vishuddhi kshetram, the breath will run out and
you will immediately start exhalation. Exhale from vishuddhi kshetram to
bindu and then down the []{#part0052.xhtml_page_310} spine from ajna to
swadhisthana chakra to complete one round.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This kriya should actually be practised for 59 rounds, but if
introversion starts to occur before you have completed the rounds,
discontinue the practice and go on to the next kriya.
:::

::: {.class1508 lang="en-us"}
[Practice note]{.class5829-0} [: If desired, mental repetition of the
chakra and kshetram can also be performed.]{.class-4}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[15: Sushumna Darshan (inner visualization of the chakras)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class3591 lang="en-us"}
For chakra visualization refer to the diagrams of each chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana. Close the eyes and
breathe normally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
There is no relation between the breath and awareness in this kriya.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring the awareness to mooladhara. Imagine a pencil, and with that
pencil draw a square at mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Draw the largest possible inverted equilateral triangle within that
square. Then make a circle touching all the four corners of that square.
Prepare four petals, one for each side of the square.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring your awareness to swadhisthana. Prepare a circle there with the
same radius as the one at mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Draw six petals around the edge of the circle, and a crescent moon
inside the bottom of the circle.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now come to manipura. Draw a circle, and then make the biggest possible
inverted triangle to fit this circle. In the centre draw a ball of fire.
Make ten petals around the circle.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Raise the consciousness to anahata.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Draw two triangles there, one triangle pointed upward and the other
inverted. They are interlaced, both crossing each other. Surround them
by by a circle with twelve petals.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Then come to vishuddhi. Draw a circle, and place a smaller circle within
the circle, like a drop of nectar. Make sixteen petals around that
circle.
:::

::: {#part0052.xhtml_page_311 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
Move up to ajna. Make a circle and inside it write a big Sanskrit
![](image3605.jpg){.class3606} . Prepare two large petals, one on the
right and one on the left side of the circle.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
At bindu draw a crescent moon with a very tiny circle above it.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Reach sahasrara. Prepare a circle there, and make the largest possible
upward pointing triangle within that circle.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
There are 1000 petals all around the circle.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to see at one glance all the chakras in their proper places.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
If it is very difficult to see them all together, then see only two
chakras on the first day and add one more to your visualization each day
until all appear together.
:::

::: class3615-1
![](image3614.jpg){.class3615-0 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[16: Prana Ahuti (infusing the divine prana)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Close the eyes and breathe normally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Feel the soft touch of a divine hand lying on your head. The hand is
infusing subtle prana into your body and mind and the prana is
travelling down from sahasrara through the spinal passage.
:::

::: {#part0052.xhtml_page_312 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
You may experience it as a wave of cold, heat energy, electric current,
or as a stream of wind or liquid.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Its passage will result in vibrations, shocks, jerks or ticking
sensations which course through you.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When the prana has reached mooladhara, then immediately go on to the
next kriya without waiting to experience the prana a second time.
:::

::: class3626-0
![](image3625.jpg){.class3626-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[17: Utthan (raising the kundalini)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sit in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Keep the eyes closed throughout and breathe normally.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Bring your awareness to mooladhara chakra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Try to visualize it clearly and notice all details.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
You will see a black shivalingam made of a smoky gaseous substance.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The bottom and top of the lingam are cut off, and circled around it is a
red baby snake.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This red baby snake is trying to uncoil itself so it can move upward
through sushumna.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As it struggles to release itself and ascends, it makes an angry hissing
sound.
:::

::: {#part0052.xhtml_page_313 .class1499 lang="en-us"}
The tail of the snake will remain fixed at the bottom of the
shivalingam, but the head and body may move upward and come back down
again.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Sometimes both the shivalingam and the snake may shift their position in
the body, so you may even visualize them for a time at ajna or
sahasrara.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The head of the snake is very wide, having the same breadth as your
body, but it is not a cobra.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After some time, you may feel your body contract. This will be followed
by a sensation of bliss.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When this occurs go on to the next kriya.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[18: Swaroopa Darshan (the vision of your Self)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Remain sitting in siddhasana/siddha yoni asana or padmasana and do not
open the eyes.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Become aware of the physical body.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Your body is completely motionless, and you maintain total awareness of
this fact.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be sure that you are completely steady, like a rock.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When you are absolutely sure of your bodily steadiness, you should also
become aware of your natural breath.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Watch the constant flow of your breath, but be sure your body remains
steady.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Your body will start to become stiff.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As it becomes stiffer, your awareness will shift completely to your
breathing; however, the body will continue to become stiffer and stiffer
of its own accord.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When your body has become as rigid as a stone, and it is beyond your
control to move it even if you tried, then go on to the next kriya.
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[19: Linga Sanchalana (astral conduction)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Remain still in your stiffened asana with the eyes closed. Due to the
stiffness of your body, your breathing will have automatically become
ujjayi breathing, and khechari mudra will have been formed.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Be totally aware of your breathing.
:::

::: class3657-0
![](image3656.jpg){#page_314 .class3657-1 lang="en-us"}
:::

::: {.class1642 lang="en-us"}
You will notice that with each inhalation your body seems to be
expanding, and with each exhalation your body appears to be contracting.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It is peculiar though, because your physical body is not moving; it is
still and as stiff as a statue.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
It is your astral body that you experience expanding and contracting.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you observe this contraction and expansion process, it will gradually
become more and more pronounced.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
After some time you will begin to lose awareness of the physical body,
and you will only be observing the astral body directly.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
However, the degree of contraction will become more pronounced.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Eventually you will reach a stage where, on contraction, the astral body
reduces to a single point of light.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
When this occurs, discontinue the kriya immediately and go on to the
next.
:::

[]{#part0053.xhtml}

::: {#part0053.xhtml_page_315 .class3286 lang="en-us"}
DHYANA PRACTICE
:::

::: {.class1497 lang="en-us"}
[20: Dhyana (meditation)]{.class-3}
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
You have realized your astral body as a single point of light.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
Now look closer at that point of light and you will see it take the form
of a golden egg.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As you watch this golden egg, it will begin to expand.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
The golden egg is luminous and glowing intensely; however, it does not
give off any rays of light.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
As the golden egg becomes larger, it will begin to take on the same
shape as that of your astral and physical bodies.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This form, however, is not a material or even a subtle form.
:::

::: {.class1499 lang="en-us"}
This form is glowing light.
:::

::: {.class1564 lang="en-us"}
It is your causal self.
:::

[]{#part0054.xhtml}

::: {#part0054.xhtml_page_316 .class3687 lang="en-us"}
[Kundalini Research](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5900)
:::

::: {.class3689 lang="en-us"}
[Compiled by]{.class5827-0}\
Dr Swami Shankardevananda Saraswati MBBS (Syd)
:::

[]{#part0055.xhtml}

::: {#part0055.xhtml_page_319 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[39](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5880)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Introduction](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5880)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[W]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} e have seen time and again that the words and
teachings of many of the yogis, saints and sages from all ages have been
recently verified by modern science. It has been our function to fit
together the bits and pieces of research and to point out:
:::

::: {.class793 lang="en-us"}
[1. The overlap between modern science and yoga,]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class793 lang="en-us"}
[2. How the various pieces fit together to give us an expanded concept
of man,]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class793 lang="en-us"}
[3. What directions research can take in order to design and analyze
research in the light of yogic psychophysiology.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[One of the great traps in attempting to research yoga is to design
experiments without a thorough knowledge of yoga itself. This is like
looking at only a small part of the whole, just as the six blind 'wise'
men, who each examined a different part of an elephant and then
pronounced their judgements based on these limitations, could never
understand the whole elephant and how it looked. Yogic training requires
many years and the skilled guidance of a master to discover its basic
principles, its mode of application, and to prepare oneself for the
experiences arising from this training.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
The totality of man
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Perhaps the outstanding feature of yoga is its ability to give us a more
total picture of who we are, to put the various elements into a simpler
and at the same time more sophisticated []{#part0055.xhtml_page_320} and
more expanded perspective. Yoga also teaches us that within us all there
is a vital power, a basic essence, whose thread can be seen running
through life, unmeasurable by even the most sophisticated machines, but
palpable and motivating our living, breathing, thinking, body and mind.
We can see its effects and measure the forms and changes of this subtle
energy as it enters and interacts with the physical domain, in the
nerves, in the chemical and intracellular processes and in the flows and
pressures of the body. However, the energy itself is still undefined
scientifically.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Through yogic sadhana we can experience the subtle energy, called prana
or kundalini, which underlies all matter. This experience is a
transformative one, which makes the subtle more tangible and real than
the material and so-called solid, physical universe. It shifts our
perspective, broadens our awareness and awakens our consciousness, our
higher and greater self. It awakens us to the fact that within us all is
an immortal and eternal essence, full of knowledge, bliss and
truth.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[The very fact that such an experience exists alters our direction and
purpose. We see that we are here not only for sensual and mundane
satisfaction, but for a higher and greater destiny. This ultimate goal
of yoga must always be remembered when we are researching yoga, for we
know that yoga can give us relaxation, alter our brain waves and
hormonal secretions, endow us with health, induce concentration and
better memory, help us to develop better human interrelationships and to
enjoy everything we do, to have fun and fulfil ourselves in a balanced,
healthy way. However, we must see that these things, though they are all
worthy and good in themselves, are not the ultimate goal of yoga, but
are side-effects of our pursuit of higher awareness and deeper knowledge
of the truth of our existence. To pursue these things in themselves is
another trap, a trick of the mind. For they do not exist by themselves
but are the outcome of a complete process of living. The yogic process
of total development of body, mind and spirit, ida, pingala
and]{.class-0} []{#part0055.xhtml_page_321 .class-0} [sushumna, is the
most systematic way to attain these things and more.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Yoga is not a science of healing and does not need to look into the
negative side of existence. The teachings tell us to practise and
emphasize the good, positive and healthy in us and automatically we will
be healthy and happy. There is nothing difficult to understand in this.
If we emphasize exercise, moderation, good lifestyle, relaxation,
meditation and self-discipline, then we are sure to achieve something
worthwhile in life. Research into relaxation, meditation, asana and
pranayama continues to demonstrate that yoga exerts real changes in the
body and mind, that it can only be a worthwhile addition to our lives if
performed under guidance and done correctly. However, we must remember
that it is much more than that, and that all our achievements are
ultimately, and in the last analysis, useless if we do not transform the
quality of our awareness.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Yoga tells us to awaken our minds, to develop the energy within
ourselves so that we can attain a much greater, fuller and more total
existence. Evidence is piling up to show that there is a psychic side to
our lives, that the mental and intangible is far from imaginary, but is
powered by an energy, a subtle force which can be tapped and developed
and which can totally change and transform the more physical side of our
lives. There is also evidence that awareness and consciousness can be
independent from the body and this is coming from studies into physics
and the nature of energy in our universe.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Purpose of this section
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
In this section we are more concerned with delineating the research into
energy than into consciousness. We are concerned with the research into
kundalini rather than with the awareness side of things. We must take it
for granted that awareness exists. Research into the energy side of yoga
shows us that there is a physically based energy in the body which also
has a psychic dimension. This fits the yogic description
[]{#part0055.xhtml_page_322} of prana, whose ultimate and maximum form
is that of kundalini.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Many times we have been amazed to hear the stories of yogis and saints
and have been awed by reading the ancient and universal teachings of
yoga, to realize that they are applicable even today. Often we have
wondered how yogis developed this science in the first place. Obviously
it has come from a profound and unusual experience, beyond the capacity
of the normal person to achieve or even understand without practising
yoga.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Satyananda Saraswati is one of those who has reached
transcendental heights and come back to tell us about kundalini in
scientific terms. He has spoken about the kundalini phenomenon and has
laid down the fundamentals of kundalini yoga in a succinct, precise,
profound and yet easily understandable and systematic manner, as has
been done in this book. He has told us many things about the functions
of the body, for example, that the right nostril connects to the left
brain, and the left nostril to the right brain, which, in 1983, was
verified by researchers at the Salk Institute in America (see]{.class-0}
[[chapter 42]{.class-0}](#part0058.xhtml){.class5828-4} [). Through his
own internal experiences he has seen that most of us do not use our
potential and that within the brain there are unused areas of potential
energy, psychic awareness and total knowledge. It is actually possible
to experience the brain from inside. The source is within us, however,
we have not connected the various centres and circuits to the main
switches and the main generator. The way to do this, Swami Satyananda
tells us, is through kundalini yoga.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Often Swami Satyananda has referred to the works of researchers as a
means of validating and expressing the kundalini experience in easily
understandable scientific terms, and to show that there are many people
working on this most important aspect of life. Much of their research is
outlined here in simple terms. This research represents pioneering
efforts to delineate the broader function of man. No doubt, in the
future, new machines and methods will have]{.class-0}
[]{#part0055.xhtml_page_323 .class-0} [to be developed, for we are
seeing only the bare beginnings of yogic research at this time. However,
the efforts of these researchers will be remembered and will set the
course for more sophisticated, scientifically acceptable
research.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class202 lang="en-us"}
[One thing is sure, science and yoga have been running parallel and in
the same direction and are now beginning to converge towards a meeting
point which promises to transform society. The concept of kundalini and
the higher sciences is becoming more widely known and respected and more
and more people are taking up its practice. This book and this section
are an offering to help you to see kundalini in a more total and easily
understood manner, to give researchers guidelines and perspective, and
to help you achieve the kundalini experience as a reality in your
life.]{.class-0}
:::

[]{#part0056.xhtml}

::: {#part0056.xhtml_page_324 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[40](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5961)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Kundalini, Fact not
Fiction](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5961)
:::

::: {.class3722 lang="en-us"}
As one opens the door with a key, so the yogi should open the gate to
liberation with the kundalini. The great goddess sleeps, closing with
her mouth, the opening through which one can ascend to the brahmarandhra
. . . to that place where there is neither pain nor suffering. The
kundalini sleeps above the kanda . . . she gives liberation to the yogi
and bondage to the fool. He who knows kundalini, knows yoga. The
kundalini, it is said, is coiled like a serpent. He who can induce her
to move is liberated.
:::

::: {.class3724 lang="en-us"}
---[Hatha Yoga Pradipika]{.class5827-0} (ch. 3, v. 105--111)
:::

::: {.class873 lang="en-us"}
With our present limited state of consciousness, bound by sense
experiences which become dull and monotonous through endless repetition,
and unable to break out of our tensions, problems and anxieties, modern
man is facing both a material and spiritual crisis. This crisis is a
two-edged sword. Kundalini both binds and liberates. On the one hand it
is 'bad', for it creates anxiety and depression and has precipitated a
plague of psychosomatic disease and suffering unparalleled in former
times. On the other hand, it is 'good', a blessing in disguise which is
forcing us to change and grow, to evolve ourselves at individual and
social levels.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[We are witnessing a tremendous upsurge of interest in yoga, meditation
and spiritual values. There has been a revival of the yogic lifestyle
and knowledge. Yoga and]{.class-0} []{#part0056.xhtml_page_325 .class-0}
[related sciences are now recognized as valuable tools within the
healing profession and have added tremendous depth and height, a new
dimension to psychology and philosophy. Scientists have been inspired to
probe deeper into the mysteries of yoga, to investigate the means by
which it works and to make the teachings of the ancient rishis and yogis
more readily understood and expressed in modern scientific terminology.
We are seeing that science is not actually discovering anything new, but
is substantiating the ancient knowledge of the yogis.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Scientific investigation into yoga and the allied sciences has made
this knowledge more accessible by incorporating it into a whole new set
of therapeutic techniques and new methods to develop our potential, for
example, biofeedback, autogenic training, mind control techniques,
psychic healing, and a myriad of other similar processes. New branches
of medicine have come into being, and the recognition of mind, begun by
Freud in the early part of the twentieth century, has finally filtered
down into common acceptance. Stress medicine and psychosomatic medicine
are examples of our deeper understanding of this interaction of energy,
mind and body, an understanding developed through our rediscovery of
yoga.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[In an effort to penetrate the mysteries of prana shakti, the physical
side of psychic energy, and chitta, the mental side of psychic energy, a
few respected and eminent pioneers, honouring the rigorous demands of
the scientific method, have accumulated a solid core of evidence which
explains in scientific terms the phenomenon of psychic energy and
validates the teachings of yogis. Science has substantiated the yogic
knowledge that a subtle energy exists which is body-based and has both
physical and psychic properties. This energy, which powers our awareness
and transforms and expands our conscious dimensions, is not just a myth
or idea; it is not a metaphysical concept, but a fact. Kundalini is
defined as the ultimate, most intense form of this energy, which lies
dormant within each and every one of us.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {#part0056.xhtml_page_326 .class185 lang="en-us"}
Parapsychology
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Phenomena such as telepathy, psychic healing, psychokinesis (the moving
of matter by mind power), dowsing, telegnosis (psychic reading of
history and association of objects), and other paranormal events, are
receiving serious attention from the more pioneering members of the
international science community as a means of understanding the
relationship of energy and consciousness.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Scientists in the USA, UK, Germany, Holland, Scandinavia and Australia
have taken the lead from scientists of the Soviet Union, many of whom
are financed by their governments. Called bioelectronics or paraphysics
in some circles, this field of study is generally known as]{.class-0}
[parapsychology.]{.class5827-1}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[In Czechoslovakia it is known as]{.class-0}
[psychotronics]{.class5827-1} [, and one of the leading Czech
researchers in this field is Dr Zdenek Rejdak, whose association with
Swami Satyananda began in the early 1970s when he stayed at the Bihar
School of Yoga. Speaking in Japan at the fifth annual conference of the
International Association for Religion and Parapsychology in 1976, Dr
Rejdak defined psychotronics, and therefore, the whole field of
parapsychology as: "The science which, in an interdisciplinary fashion,
studies the distant interactions between living organisms and their
environment, internal and external, and the energetic processes
underlying these manifestations in order to supplement and widen man's
understanding of the laws of nature."]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Psychic energy
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Psychic energy has been found to affect a whole range of laboratory
equipment, from voltmeters to Geiger counters to magnetometers. Yet this
does not mean that psychic energy is electrical, magnetic or
radioactive. Rather, it seems to both encompass and go beyond these
properties. Most researchers agree with the Russians who state that
psychic energy may have its origin in electrical activity, but the
nature of the energy is entirely different. However, yogis state that
prana is the substratum of our material universe, interpenetrating
[]{#part0056.xhtml_page_327} and organizing all matter and being the
common ground for all energy. They see prana from a different and higher
perspective.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[It is also generally accepted by scientists that psychic energy, most
widely known as]{.class-0} [bioenergy]{.class5827-1} [, is body-based
and affects both the physical and mental spheres as indicated by yogis.
It has also been measured as a force field surrounding the body up to a
distance of twelve feet by Yale neuropsychiatrist, Dr Leonard
Ravitz.]{.class-0} []{#part0056.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5826
.class-0}
[[1]{.class-0}](#part0068.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5923){.class5834-0}
[This seems to support the yogic concept of the subtle pranic body which
interpenetrates and is interdependent with the physical structure,
motivating it to function.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[There is considerable support for this hypothesis, gathered from the
monitoring of the physiological changes experienced by psychics during
laboratory tests of paranormal events. For instance, as part of his
usual experimental procedure, Dr Grenady Sergeyev of the A.A. Utkomskii
Physiological Institute (a Leningrad military laboratory), took readings
of the brain waves, heartbeat and pulse rates of Neyla Mikhailova during
her numerous demonstrations of psychokinesis.]{.class-0}
[]{#part0056.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5915 .class-0}
[[2]{.class-0}](#part0068.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A6021){.class5834-0}
[He found that while Mikhailova was causing objects to move without
touching them, his instruments recorded a tremendous vibration
throughout her body and its surrounding force field which pulsed in the
direction of her gaze. Her heart and brain waves also pulsed in unison
with this energy vibration, indicating that the energy Mikhailova used
in her psychic feats is intimately connected with her whole
body.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Reports go on to state that: "After doing these tests, Mrs. Mikhailova
was utterly exhausted. There was almost no pulse. She'd lost close to
four pounds in half an hour. The EEG (brain wave pattern) showed intense
emotional excitement. There was high blood sugar and the endocrine
system was disturbed. The whole organism was weakened as if from a
tremendous stress reaction. She had lost the sensation of taste, had
pains in her arms and legs, couldn't coordinate and felt
dizzy."]{.class-0} []{#part0056.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5945
.class-0}
[[3]{.class-0}](#part0068.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5849){.class5834-0}
:::

::: {#part0056.xhtml_page_328 .class179 lang="en-us"}
[At one time, after making a seven hour film of her abilities,
Mikhailova was temporarily blind. Other Soviet investigators have
recorded changes in brain wave patterns which coincide with the
reception of telepathic signals, and researchers in the USA have shown
that the volume of blood in the body alters during telepathic
interactions.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[This evidence leaves no doubt that psychic energy, or bioenergy, is
from the body and is the same energy activating every aspect of
metabolism, from functioning of the glands, to the brain and heart. It
is the power behind the emotions and senses. At the same time, prana,
though based on and affecting the physical structure and function, has a
wider range of properties and is associated with clairvoyance,
clairaudience and other forms of extrasensory perception. It has a
mental or psychic component and is both gross and subtle.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Psychic energy can affect matter without any apparent physical
intermediary or medium. There is some undetectable energy at work which
we cannot measure though we can see its results. It can even be used in
healing. Sister Dr Justa Smith, in America, has demonstrated that
psychic energy affects enzymes.]{.class-0}
[]{#part0056.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5927 .class-0}
[[4]{.class-0}](#part0068.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A6016){.class5834-0}
[She has found that trypsin, a digestive enzyme which is damaged and
decreases activity when exposed to ultraviolet light, increases activity
when exposed to a high intensity magnetic field. When a water damaged
trypsin solution was held in the hands of a recognized psychic healer
for 72 minutes, trypsin increased its activity.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[R. Yaeger has shown that when a practitioner of kundalini yoga
performed certain pranayama techniques and then sat next to an onion for
15 minutes with his hands in a fixed position, about two feet from the
experimental plant, cell division, and therefore metabolic energy
increased by 108%.]{.class-0}
[]{#part0056.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5832 .class-0}
[[5]{.class-0}](#part0068.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A6013){.class5834-0}
[A control subject sitting in the same position, but without doing
pranayama, had no effects on the plant.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[We have clear evidence from these experiments that there is a new kind
of psychic physiological energy that fits the description of prana and
kundalini as set forth in the yogic texts and verbal
traditions.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {#part0056.xhtml_page_329 .class185 lang="en-us"}
Summary
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Modern science has been able to ascertain that psychic energy is a real
and physically-based phenomenon. Though it does not fall into the known
categories of modern science, its effects can be experienced and
recorded repeatedly. No one really doubts its existence. What it is and
how it functions, its relationship to our body and mind and its
potential use as an evolutionary tool require further research from
scientists who will find guidelines in the perspectives and experiences
of dedicated yogis.
:::

::: {.class202 lang="en-us"}
[Through this, we will be better able to understand the relationship of
mind and body and this will have tremendous repercussions on studies
into psychosomatic medicine, psychology and other important fields. As
we ourselves learn to appreciate that great joy and good health which
comes from developing and being sensitive to psychic energy, a large and
forgotten area of our being, we will extend our possibilities, develop
our innate potential and speed up our spiritual evolution.]{.class-0}
:::

[]{#part0057.xhtml}

::: {#part0057.xhtml_page_330 .class216 lang="en-us"}
[41](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5939)
:::

::: {.class218 lang="en-us"}
[Defining the Nadis](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5939)
:::

::: {.class220 lang="en-us"}
[Y]{.class220-kfx-dropcap} oga and tantra lay down one of the most
complete systems for a practical understanding of the human condition.
Tantra supplies the philosophy, the theoretical approach. Yoga supplies
techniques by which we can validate this philosophy through our own
personal experience and thus attain higher knowledge. Tantra is
therefore a living philosophy and not just a system of endless
intellectual speculation unable to deliver the truth and leaving more
questions unanswered than answered. It is also a very potent method by
which we can realize ourselves in totality, and attain union, ultimate
freedom and fulfilment.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Perhaps the greatest contribution of tantra to the modern world will be
its ability not just to define the mind and put it into perspective, but
to deliver techniques by which we can experience the mind itself and
eventually transcend it through the awakening of kundalini. Modern
medicine and psychology, for example, will greatly benefit from tantra's
fundamental, basic components of body, mind and spirit -- pingala, ida
and sushumna. These flows of energy make up our total human personality
and are derived from the ultimate polarity of our macrocosmic universe
into Shiva and Shakti, consciousness and energy.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[In trying to understand the manifestations of these forces in our body,
and for research purposes, in trying to prove the reality of the
existence of the nadis, we have to understand]{.class-0}
[]{#part0057.xhtml_page_331 .class-0} [that they are not physical,
measurable, dissectable structures within our physical body, but are the
basic energies which underlie and motivate life and
consciousness.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[It is important to understand exactly what nadis are before we either
try to prove their existence or disprove it. When we achieve certain
states of consciousness we can see that nadis are, as yogis described
them, flows of energy which we can visualize at the psychic level as
having distinct channels, light, colour, sound and other
characteristics. At the same time, however, these nadis underlie, and
can be seen mirrored in, all bodily functions and processes. There is no
separation between the nadis, the body and the mind; they are one and
the same thing.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
The duality of life
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
In many of the oriental philosophies, the entire universe is seen as a
separation into two great, polarized forces, Shiva and Shakti, which are
interdependent and opposite, but complementary. The universe hangs as a
kind of web of interacting energies, suspended and functioning within
the framework of tensions developed by the fundamental polarity. Carl
Jung stated, "natural processes are phenomena of energy constantly
arising out of a 'less probable'
state."[]{#part0057.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5971}
[1](#part0068.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5998){.class5834-1} This
apparent dualism is actually a unified, holistic process from another
level of consciousness, but at our own level we see it from a
fragmented, limited and partial perspective.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[We see polarity everywhere we look, in nature, within ourselves and
within our mind. Moving from macrocosmic to microcosmic to atomic, at
every level, two great principles or forces can be seen at work
motivating our universe; light and dark, positive and negative, male and
female. All other forces are seen to be an outcome of these two main
forces. It seems amazing to us that things can be so simple and yet so
profound; however, to the enlightened mind, the universe and man is just
so.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[All of life, therefore, has two main aspects upon which all of our
perception, activity and experience are based. Our]{.class-0}
[]{#part0057.xhtml_page_332 .class-0} [mind and body are the outcome of
two main forms or modes of energy interacting and creating endless
manifestations in the universe of our body. For example, we have a right
and left brain, a parasympathetic and sympathetic nervous system, an
anabolic and catabolic metabolism, a conscious and unconscious mind. We
are poised between life and death and our whole existence is a struggle
to retain balance between these two forces.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
Ida and pingala
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Yogis realized the existence of these forces and understood their
relationship. They said that man has three main flows of energy, which
they called the nadis, ida, pingala and sushumna, and which have been
roughly translated as mind, body, and spirit. The third flow is the
result of the balanced interaction of the first two. They also said that
man functions mainly in the first two areas of body and mind, pingala
and ida, the third aspect being dormant until it is stimulated by yoga
or some other discipline.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Ida and pingala are roughly translated as mind and body. Though this is
true at one level, when we are discussing the polarization of the total
individual, the body and mind are themselves each polarized. We have to
understand, however, that the nadis are not structures but are
functional relationships and are really different sides of the same
coin. Yogis did not describe the nadis in terms of structures, though
structure exists to handle them. They described them in terms of
energy,]{.class-0} [prana]{.class5827-1} [, vital and life-giving for
pingala, and]{.class-0} [chitta]{.class5827-1} [, consciousness and
knowing for ida. The attributes of the nadis are summarized
below:]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Pingala can be defined as the dynamic, active, masculine, positive,
yang energy within our personality. It has a physical and mental side.
Its material qualities are light, heat, solar, energy accumulating,
creative, organizing, focused (centripetal) and contractive. The
positive, dynamic mental side within Freud's system is Eros, the
pleasure principle, and in Jung's system it is the conscious
personality, the rational,]{.class-0} []{#part0057.xhtml_page_333
.class-0} [discriminating side. We can say that pingala is psychosomatic
energy, outwardly directed, mind acting on body to motivate the organs
of action, the karmendriyas. It is the basic energy of life.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Ida is the energy within the personality which is passive, receptive,
feminine, negative, yin. At the physical level it is dark, cold, lunar,
energy dissipating, disorganizing, entropic, expansive (centrifugal) and
relaxing. At the mental plane Freud called it Thanatos, the death
instinct, and Jung called it anima, the unconscious female within,
emotional, feeling, intuitive and non-discriminating, the background on
which the differences can be seen and which unifies. This is the
somopsychic aspect of man, where energy is inwardly directed, and the
body acts on the mind. Ida controls the sense organs or jnanendriyas
and, therefore, gives us knowledge and awareness of the world we live
in.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
The third force
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Another force exists in nature which is little understood or even
appreciated, but which is of vital importance. It is a fact that when
two opposing forces are equal and balanced, a third force arises. Strike
a match on a matchbox and you create fire, bring positive and negative
currents together and you can work machinery, unite body and mind and a
third force called sushumna, spiritual energy, arises. This is one of
the aims of yoga, because only when sushumna awakens can the super power
of kundalini, this maximum force, ascend safely to fuel, power and
create cosmic consciousness. Sushumna is a high tension power line, and
ida and pingala carry the domestic lines to power the basic necessities.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Carl Jung outlined the tantric view when he described the driving force
of self-realization, which he called 'individuation', as a dialectical
interaction between the opposites, beginning with conflict and
culminating in synthesis and integration. When perfect balance is
achieved, stabilized and perfected, a state of dynamic peace is also
achieved, which is a paradox, a union of opposites, the]{.class-0}
[]{#part0057.xhtml_page_334 .class-0} [synthesis of doing and not doing,
a totally new way of perceiving and experiencing life.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Few of us realize this third, spiritualized state and most of us
oscillate from one state to another. Every 90 to 180 minutes ida and
pingala alternate their dominance and only for a few seconds or minutes
does sushumna come into potential being. It is the goal of all yogic
techniques to balance and harmonize ida and pingala, life force and
conscious awareness, so that they join at ajna chakra to create the
inner light of knowledge and bliss and reveal the truth.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[In order to balance the flows of energy, yoga prescribes various
techniques, asana, pranayama, shatkarma and meditation, which activate
either ida, pingala or sushumna. This does not mean we are activating
one structure but are, via yoga, able to manipulate the energies
underlying the three possible modes of existence.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class185 lang="en-us"}
The functional modes
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
Nadis are flows of energy which move through each and every part of our
body, the subtle counterpart of the physical flows such as nervous
energy and blood. All of the thousands of nadis in the body are based on
ida and pingala which spiral around the spinal cord. These are the basic
two modes of function on which all of our bodily and mental processes
