circuits within the body. I somehow suspect that we go along on a number
of different levels of consciousness]{.class-0}
[]{#part0064.xhtml_page_408 .class-0} [at the same time. Sometimes we
have dreams of total experiences of something that is going to occur in
three or four months' time. That means time, instead of being a
longitudinal thing, is a vertical thing. How do we explain that in our
neurophysiological framework? There are a lot of experiences that are
difficult to explain scientifically. I don't think that necessarily
means that a physiological explanation is invalid.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[These days it is possible to measure certain physical manifestations of
chakras and the dissociated chakras. Maybe you could get a personality
break of a person who was obviously into a certain chakra and test the
activation of that chakra. I think the energy around the chakra is
easily explainable in that it is the energy that would be given off by
the activated field.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : In terms of circuits, some of
the chakras have more receptive properties, especially in mooladhara and
ajna, whilst certain chakras seem to be more expressive, such as
swadhisthana and manipura.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Probably it is associated with the
jnanendriyas and karmendriyas (sensory and motor nerves).
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : All the chakras must have a
dual purpose: there must be a receptive and active side to them. For
example, ajna is receptive to psychic and intuitive energy, but it also
transmits at the subtle, telepathic level. Vishuddhi, which expresses
and communicates that intuition at the verbal level, simultaneously
expresses compassion felt through anahata, and also expresses the
experiences felt through manipura and swadhisthana. All chakras have a
two-way channel and that is because of ida and pingala.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : I think that vishuddhi expresses the
qualities of the other chakras only as an agent of their quality,
because the other chakras will express energy in a different way. If you
are with a person who is loving, especially if you get close, you can
feel the love pouring out. Therefore, anahata is expressing in that way,
but I think that anahata would use vishuddhi chakra to say the words
that go with it.
:::

::: {#part0064.xhtml_page_409 .class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : Yes, the energy flows through
the other chakras, so the activation of one chakra affects them all and
modifies them according to its major harmonic, but in its own way.
Manipura and swadhisthana chakras would then become love dominant if
anahata becomes active. All the other chakras would then line themselves
up with anahata.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Manipura chakra is an expressive
chakra and if you feel high in manipura, then it would tend to flow out
love more than feel the experience of love, which is anahata.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : There is a definite connection
between mooladhara and ajna. Also, there appears to be a connection
between swadhisthana, vishuddhi and bindu, a very direct connection, and
lalana, which is a sub-chakra of vishuddhi. Then it seems that manipura
and anahata are also related. This intimate connection between the
chakras is symbolized by the seven candles on the Hebrew candlestand
(menorah). This is a representation of how chakras are interacting, but
actually it is a much more complicated diagram in which all chakras
interact with each other. We can regard mooladhara and swadhisthana as
being tamasic chakras, manipura and anahata as being predominantly
rajasic, and vishuddhi and ajna as being sattwic. These pairs function
together. Vishuddhi and ajna, for example, are connected on a receptive,
expressive merger, one being active and the other being receptive.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : But I see rajasic and tamasic
qualities being in each of the chakras and I see the chakras as being
horizontal rather than a vertical ladder form. They all have qualities
from rajasic, right through to sattwic.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : That is also true. Some people
think the word tamasic carries moralistic connotations.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : In the context of evolution, is the
bliss that the yogi experiences any different to the bliss of orgasm? It
might be at a more highly evolved level. Is the selfish love of a mother
for her child, to the exclusion of all other
[]{#part0064.xhtml_page_410} children, anything more than just a lower
level of transcendental love?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : In his article on kundalini,
Carl Jung says that from above manipura chakra you leave the whole
sphere of the earth behind, the individuality -- and the diaphragm which
lies at the manipura level could be an important anatomical separating
component as far as the chakras are concerned. The movement away from
individual love towards universal love takes place at that point just
above the diaphragm -- anahata chakra.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : It is very likely that these
different opinions are all right. The mountain looks different from
different angles, but from above you see all the people looking at the
same mountain. The problem comes when you go back down to earth and talk
to all the individual people. It is very difficult to describe what you
experienced when you saw the whole mountain. This is why we get so many
different opinions, philosophies and religions.
:::

::: {.class4233 lang="en-us"}
MOOLADHARA AND SWADHISTHANA CHAKRAS
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : Can you discuss the nerve
complexes associated with mooladhara and swadhisthana chakras?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Well, for all of these segments
there are somatic nerves, which deal with the sensory input and the
voluntary motor output, and also there are the autonomic nerves, divided
into sympathetic and parasympathetic. And usually there is an
appropriate endocrine gland for each segment, like the pineal, pituitary
and thyroid. The exception is mooladhara, and to date, medical science
has not found an endocrine gland associated with it. This of course does
not mean that one will not be discovered in the future.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Let us try to work out the psychophysiological aspects of mooladhara.
In the male it is actually associated with the base of the penis and
with the female, the cervix. So it has a very deep-rooted sexual
link.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {#part0064.xhtml_page_411 .class179 lang="en-us"}
[If you repeat a mooladhara chakra mantra and you concentrate in that
area somewhere, you will feel a certain vibration occurring. Now what is
the mantra doing? Is it stimulating some physiological organ, or is it
some sort of occult stimulation? Is it stimulating a physical organ or
is it activating a lot of energy which seems to appear in a certain
place which we call a chakra? I think it is perhaps the last one of
these.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : I believe that the mooladhara
trigger point and the place of actual experience may be different, but
the general location of mooladhara chakra is certainly in the perineum;
it is clearly felt in that area. If it is felt higher, then it is not
mooladhara chakra, it is swadhisthana. Either the mantra is wrong or the
vibration is stimulating something else which is more receptive and
reactive.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Is there a physiological basis for
this? It is quite possible that the repetition of a mantra is
stimulating the spinal cord. You can certainly feel it in the area being
stimulated and it is not only there, because all the fibres that are
coming out from the body are stimulated. Therefore, no matter at what
level you stimulate your spinal cord, no matter what chakra is
stimulated, you are going to collect the fibres from so called
mooladhara chakra. At swadhisthana chakra you will also get the
mooladhara chakra fibres; at manipura you get the mooladhara fibres back
to swadhisthana and manipura as well -- and all the way up. Mooladhara
chakra is always there in the act because its fibres come from the
lowest part.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : Could we consider the sexual
energy of mooladhara and its possible transmutations?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : This basic sexual energy that Gopi
Krishna has written about is actually the sattwic or subtle essence
which can be perceived when the consciousness becomes very sensitive.
This is the essence of the kundalini experience, the sublimation of
sexual energy, the basic life force which is the source of all
generation, regeneration []{#part0064.xhtml_page_412} and reproduction.
Gopi Krishna felt what he was seeing was semen being converted into
energy and distributing itself throughout the body. I feel that what he
was perceiving was a clairvoyant view of energy given off by the simple
nerve fibres in those organs he was talking about. However, he
identified it as semen because that is what is written in the
scriptures. I do not know what women are supposed to have, he did not
mention that and I do not think the scriptures do either.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Nischalananda]{.class5824-1} : The [Hatha Yoga
Pradipika]{.class5827-0} and certain tantric texts do talk about women;
however, generally that side has been neglected. According to yoga the
sexual energy in men and women is sublimated and transmuted into the
ascent of the kundalini. The starting point is mooladhara. For some
reason, the Buddhists say that the ascent commences at manipura, not
mooladhara. How is it that the enlightened Buddha completely bypassed
the two lower chakras? Actually the whole concept of where kundalini
lies is a matter of experience. I don't think that Buddha actually said
that kundalini starts in manipura; more likely he stated that real
spiritual evolution starts from manipura. Swami Satyananda has said many
times that only when the kundalini reaches manipura is it stabilized. It
starts in mooladhara but stabilizes in manipura.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[I think this apparent discrepancy comes because of the philosophy of
Buddha who was a jnani, and he didn't get much into kundalini yoga.
Vajrayana, on the other hand, which was an offshoot of Buddhism at a
later date, is very much concerned with mooladhara. But let us get back
to the functioning of mooladhara.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : Mooladhara chakra has two basic
modes of function, one is energy depleted and the other is energy
activated. Within that system there is a sick and a healthy mooladhara.
What are the symptoms of these different states of mooladhara chakra? It
is simple -- you are either sick or healthy, balanced or unbalanced. If
you are unbalanced you are going to have ida over or under active or
[]{#part0064.xhtml_page_413} pingala over or under active. You are going
to have physical and mental symptoms, fear, insecurity and all those
things. Freud said that everyone who denies mooladhara becomes
constipated and hoards money. Every miser is constipated. These symptoms
may be mild or very extreme. In the fully awakened state they are either
going to rip you to pieces or take you to a higher awareness. So what is
the basic quality of a well functioning mooladhara chakra?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Renunciation.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : We can say that security and
renunciation are interchangeable in the mooladhara system. We can say
that in this chakra basic security is the key. Renunciation obviously
implies security and if you are secure within yourself, you don't need
any external security.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Satyadharma]{.class5824-1} : When awakening of mooladhara takes
place then there is no such problem as insecurity.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Of course, this is the state of
consciousness of an awakened mooladhara. A low energized mooladhara
chakra generally means low vitality, emotional insecurity, fear of the
future. I also think low self-esteem is involved in this. It almost
forms the syndrome of depression, although you don't necessarily have to
get the joylessness of the low energized swadhisthana chakra. If there
is low evolution and high drive in mooladhara, then you get the
ambitious person out to collect as much as he can. He can be a
multimillionaire and still accumulate all sorts of things because he
still feels insecure. The security is a state of consciousness, not a
physical reality. As mooladhara chakra starts to evolve the person
attains security, which is totally unrelated to circumstances.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[You can see varying degrees of renunciation not only between sannyasins
and the community, but within the community of sannyasins as
well.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Satyadharma]{.class5824-1} : When energies pool at mooladhara
chakra, do they stimulate or aggravate the chakras? What is the
difference between stagnation of energy and activation of the chakra?
:::

::: {#part0064.xhtml_page_414 .class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Well, I just see that the mooladhara
circuit in some people is sometimes poorly energized; the whole circuit
itself has low energization. This varies between people and varies
within people, depending upon cosmic events, the position of planets,
the weather and all sorts of things, including psychological factors
such as disappointments, hurts and threats to one's security. It varies
with each of us. Some people are very much in mooladhara; hooked on the
basic sexual aspect of mooladhara in which case they are very much
involved in money and possessions. If they are low energized, they will
still think about these things, but they will not do anything about it.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[I think you need a certain amount of energization to produce the drive
that is inherent in each chakra; the basic sexual hunting drive in
swadhisthana chakra, the territorial and dominance drive in manipura and
the nurturing drive in anahata chakra. Remember, there are two
parameters, the amount of energization of each chakra and the degree of
evolution.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[It seems that yoga practices balance the energy inherent within each of
the chakra circuits, and by virtue of eliminating the blockages
(samskaras), evolve the quality of the chakras at the same time. And of
course, if you have the grace of the guru you are on the express
line.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Satyadharma]{.class5824-1} : So does pooled energy act to block
or can it be used to activate the chakra? For example, if a person has a
lot of pooled energy in mooladhara, would that be an energy block or
could that pooled energy be utilized to activate and awaken a chakra?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : It can be used to activate it if the
psychological blockages are eliminated.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : I think there is a difference
between storage and blockage. The ability to hold or store energy takes
place consciously, whilst having an unconscious or subconscious blockage
leads to repression.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : And repression of a highly energized
chakra can produce all sorts of physical symptoms, such as
[]{#part0064.xhtml_page_415} muscle tension, malfunctioning of internal
organs, etc., as well as emotional problems.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : What are the psychological
effects of mooladhara awakening?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : As I have already said,
renunciation.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : The feeling of separation, the
beginning of your individual awareness, awakening to the fact that you
are separate from something else.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Nischalananda]{.class5824-1} : Primal alienation or something
like that.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : Do you think that the basic
energy at mooladhara is anxiety, fear, or is it insecurity?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : The basic emotion? Well, it depends
on the energization of the circuit. If there is not much energy, it will
tend to be depression and hopelessness. But if there is a lot of energy,
it will then depend upon the evolution of the chakra. If it is little
evolved, then there will be intense insecurity, which is anxiety. If it
is highly evolved there will be a sense of oneness and complete
security. Generally mooladhara is blocked to some extent in most people
and blockages may manifest as muscle tension.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[Muscle tensions are manifestations of the circuits of mental blockages,
samskaras. It is the samskaras that keep down the evolution of the
quality of consciousness that is within these chakra circuits. I think
that low evolution, muscle spasms and the maladjustments of the
organisms that are supplied by that part of the autonomic nervous system
are due to psychic tensions.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : These psychic and personality
tensions are due to various events in the environment.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : That is right. The inner unconscious
conflicts coming into conflict with certain events in the environment.
For example, if a person feels very insecure and someone steals a
valuable possession from him, he may go into an absolute frenzy. This is
opposed to the reaction of someone else who does not have the same sort
of conflicts and insecurities.
:::

::: {#part0064.xhtml_page_416 .class179 lang="en-us"}
[If a person cannot express the feeling that is involved at mooladhara,
that feeling can express itself in somatic problems like spasms of the
muscles, in autonomic problems, blood pressure, constipation, and who
knows what else, maybe functional urethritis, cystitis, colitis,
rectitis, dysmenorrhea and so on.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class4233 lang="en-us"}
PSYCHOSIS
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : Would you associate a highly
energized, low evolved mooladhara problem as the cause of manic
depression?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : I think manic depression is an
ida/pingala thing. We are in another dimension there, because a manic
person will undergo all the manifestations of a very highly energized
and controlled chakra. He will be rushing around gambling all his money
away, trying to get more, getting into all sorts of sexual exploits,
going round pushing other people around, the rajasic aspect.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Sambuddhananda]{.class5824-1} : Would you say that schizophrenia
and paranoia are related with ida and pingala imbalance?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Yes, there are people who are stuck
in ida. Ida is very much overactive. It is interesting that research
shows that the taking in of negative aspects of the environment through
the right hemisphere (ida) is paranoia. This is what paranoia is all
about. A lot of people, some of them quite highly evolved people, who
have specialized much in ida are a bit paranoid. Ida seems to have a
negative aspect about it. Even if you come into it at a high level of
consciousness, it seems to have a bit of a negative pull. If you are
going to activate your chakras, you have to make sure your ida and
pingala are balanced.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : But manic depression, psychosis
and other mental problems relate to either mooladhara or ajna because it
is only at these two points that you have the fusion of ida and pingala.
Therefore, psychosis, manic depression and all these things would seem
to relate very []{#part0064.xhtml_page_417} much to the mooladhara/ajna
circuit. If ida and pingala are coming out of mooladhara chakra, then
what would be the mechanism dealing with psychosis?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : I think that ida and pingala are
only related to the activities of the cerebral hemispheres.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : But the whole body is
controlled by the hemispheres. The whole body gets the energy. Arteries
and veins, sensory and motor nerves, right and left hemispheres are all
reflections of the ida and pingala process.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : I see ida and pingala anatomically
up here in the brain, not crossing down the spine. I believe that ida
and pingala crossing each other is a concept and a symbol of experience.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Satyadharma]{.class5824-1} : I think that awakening of mooladhara
is the beginning of psychic awareness. That is why with mooladhara
awakening, people often become disturbed.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Yes. They can get caught in the
psychic consciousness, which is the consciousness in which you have
hallucinations, etc.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : It is much more powerful than
anything they have ever experienced before.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : We slide in and out of it twice a
day anyway, even if we are not doing any formal closed eye meditation
techniques. I think if you hold the awareness at the psychic level, and
you can do it with yoga nidra, you will experience a state in which
there is thought blocking -- what is called thought disorder -- where
one thought leads on to another one that is unrelated to it and it just
goes off into the distance. Paradoxical thinking -- where two
paradoxical things can exist together, hallucinations, voices talking to
you, you see things and so forth.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : So, therefore we assume that
pingala is blocked and ida is flowing. All that stuff is coming out
through ida from mooladhara; basic subconscious material.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : At the same time there is psychic
withdrawal.
:::

::: {#part0064.xhtml_page_418 .class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : Yes, so what does that imply?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : If there is a psychic withdrawal,
then even though we appear to be in communication with the outside, in
actual fact we are still inside from the psychic point of view.
Paradoxical thinking, suspicious feelings, voices and all these things,
and not being able to keep your thoughts together on one topic for any
more than a couple of seconds; all these come from a psychic, inner
plane.
:::

::: {.class4233 lang="en-us"}
PHYSICAL DISEASES
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : What about physical disease
associated with mooladhara chakra problems? We have already talked about
constipation; this of course brings about things like haemorrhoids.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : There are many types of constipation
involved too -- of energy, emotions, information -- all inherent in
mooladhara chakra as hoarding of any type.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Gaurishankar]{.class5824-1} : What about disease?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Statistics involved in diseases in
this area tend to relate to the manipura and anahata areas, and the
diseases of hypertension, heart problems, peptic ulcers etc. I assume
many diseases of the lower excretory and reproductive organs are
associated with a malfunctioning mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : Cancer?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Yes, of the rectum and bladder.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : The helplessness associated
with it too?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : I don't know if it is all cancers we
are talking about now. I don't know if they would be segmental or not.
Hypertension, for instance, appears to be a generalized condition. It is
mainly related to the manipura chakra circuits. Cancer may well be a
generalized condition that is related to one of the chakras, perhaps
mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Paramananda]{.class5824-1} : How far can you take the
relationship between the chakras and the physical organs like the heart?
[]{#part0064.xhtml_page_419} If the heart is not functioning well and it
affects the anahata chakra which is love, can that also mean that there
is a lack of love going through that person and physically it comes out
in anahata chakra and the heart as disease?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Yes, it can be in both. If a person
has a need to receive love and it is not coming, and/or that person has
imbalanced constructions of love, then anahata problems can arise in the
form of cardiac problems such as angina, palpitations, etc.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Paramananda]{.class5824-1} : Do you think that applies to all the
chakras? If you find a particular organ not functioning in a sick
person, does it mean there is a deficiency of the qualities of the
chakra related to that part of the body?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : As a general rule, yes, but you can
get other problems as well. For instance, you can get an activation of
manipura chakra, which activates the sympathetic nervous system which
produces restriction of the coronary artery.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[There is interaction between the different chakras, and this is the
beauty of a well-taught yoga class -- it balances all these qualities,
and balance is the key to the whole thing. Rather than trying to work on
one area, which is a more specific medical style, yoga therapy works on
the whole human structure.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Muktibodhananda]{.class5824-1} : How do the physical organs
relate to the chakras and spiritual evolution?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Consider hysterectomy. Let us assume
the wrong woman is wheeled into the operating theatre and she has a
hysterectomy. This will then cut off the end organ for a lot of nerve
fibres and the atrophy will run up the nerves and eliminate the brain
centres involved in that. This is an example of a deficiency in the
organ producing changes in the centres involved, the circuit. Does that
make it any more difficult for her to realize higher aspects of
swadhisthana chakra?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : It depends how much of the
centre is lost. If she just loses the uterus and not the ovaries, for
example, all the hormonal secretions will be maintained.
[]{#part0064.xhtml_page_420} As women reach menopause they will undergo
a natural hysterectomy.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Yes, but they don't lose the nerve
endings. When the uterus is removed, because the nerve endings are
useless, they atrophy. Does this affect the associated chakras?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Nischalananda]{.class5824-1} : Swami Satyananda says it does not
make any difference if there is a vasectomy, because it is only the
physical body. I think, as regards swadhisthana for example, that if
they are already on the spiritual path and have developed some psychic
awareness, then that operation would definitely not affect them much, if
at all. If they had no background of yogic practise, then probably the
destruction of that organ would slightly hamper progress, because
initially you depend upon those organs to stimulate something,
especially in the practices of hatha and kriya yoga. If you follow the
path of bhakti or jnana yoga, of course, it makes no difference.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : If you lose one centre or two
centres, physically I think it does not hinder you because a lot of
other centres are left. There are tons of potential left within the
brain.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : To sum up, we function on physical,
emotional, mental, psychic and spiritual levels. The chakras span all
these levels. The purpose of yoga and tantra is to stimulate the chakras
at all these levels. Then, and only then, can we become healthy human
beings.
:::

::: {.class4233 lang="en-us"}
MENTAL PROBLEMS
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Sambuddhananda]{.class5824-1} : What is the cause of depression?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : I think low activation of the
swadhisthana circuit is the prime cause of depression.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : I thought it was due to low
activation in mooladhara.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Well, the qualities in both these
chakras are very close.
:::

::: {#part0064.xhtml_page_421 .class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : So what is the difference
between mooladhara and swadhisthana?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : You can see the different qualities
in the various types of anxiety you see in different people. In
psychiatry, the various forms of anxiety all come under the name of
anxiety, yet they are all different syndromes, and they are also related
to different chakra circuits. People with a low energized mooladhara
chakra are not just apprehensive about the future, they also feel
insecure about the present. They simply don't feel that this is a secure
world, and the state of consciousness they have at any time is that
things are dangerous.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[There is another type of depression which I perceived in a woman who
was forty-five years of age. Her husband had left her when she was about
thirty-five, and she led a very quiet life. But she was still pretty
energized in swadhisthana chakra. She was describing the anxiety that
she had. Through empathy I started to experience what she was
describing. It was a sort of quivering vibration going on in the pelvis.
It was a quivering all around the area of swadhisthana chakra, not
specifically genital, but all around the upper part of the pelvis. It
really was a type of anxiety.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[I gave her the general swadhisthana practices such as shalabhasana,
etc. She improved a lot. The yogic practices seemed to deactivate her
pent-up emotion. I think it was just sexual tension that she had in that
area and she was perceiving it as anxiety. She also had a fear of it
because she did not know what it was.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[There is another case of depression which is a well-known one --
butterflies in the stomach, accompanied by palpitations, which is just
activation of the sympathetic nervous system. One case I saw was a taxi
driver who had a minor accident in his cab. He got this phobia and he
couldn't get in his taxi without experiencing butterflies. In Aruba
(South America), where he lived, taxi fares are minimal so that the taxi
drivers are really hard up. This man had to employ someone else to drive
his cab for him and he was]{.class-0} []{#part0064.xhtml_page_422
.class-0} [losing money. He had been off work for six weeks. Every time
he went up to his cab he would get this terrible churning in the stomach
and he developed hypertension. He was a very dynamic Aries.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[So I thought, "What to do?" I taught him kunjal in order to get all
that energy out of manipura chakra. He did it once in the ashram and
then immediately went out and got in his cab. This type of anxiety and
depression is obviously manipura overactivity.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[There is another type of anxiety which arises through too much
thinking: "Wouldn't it be terrible if such and such happened, and if
that happens maybe something else will happen, and if that happens maybe
. . .?" People with this problem just think and think and think, until
that preoccupation produces a fear within them which is not necessarily
contained in the symptoms. That is dealt with by practising bhramari
pranayama. So within the diagnosis of anxiety there seems to be these
four types. There may be others related to the other chakras, but I have
not yet noticed them.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Nischalananda]{.class5824-1} : Maybe stuttering, loss of voice
and things like that, related to vishuddhi, can be cured by simhasana.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Exactly, tightening up of the
throat. It seems to be more related to a lack of self-confidence rather
than the feeling of anxiety. Simhasana works wonders.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[When I was in general practice, I used to do a lot of spinal
adjustments and manipulation, and after a while I specialized in spinal
problems. I did a lot of backs at that stage. I found that patients came
in clusters. I would get a lot of people with an upper cervical lesion,
migraine headaches, tightness in the neck region, with all the symptoms
of chronic sinusitis and all the other things related to upper cervical
tension.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[I found that all the people with upper cervical problems were coming in
when the moon was full, all the people with lumbar/sacral problems were
coming in when the moon was new, and in between all the others were
spread out. This is]{.class-0} []{#part0064.xhtml_page_423 .class-0}
[interesting because it is related to chakra activation. Almost before
the patient told me, I could pinpoint the exact spinal segment in which
he would be having problems. I knew according to the moon phase. This
relationship became obvious, especially towards the end of the time I
was manipulating, because I took on the symptoms of my
patients.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : This means that we need a whole
set of asanas working on all the segments of the spine.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Yes, we have them, for example,
surya namaskara. In Australia we used to use the leg lock posture for
mooladhara chakra; shalabhasana and bhujangasana for swadhisthana
chakra. These asanas are actually supposed to be for manipura chakra,
but so many people have such stiff backs that they activate swadhisthana
chakra instead. Then paschimottanasana and dhanurasana for manipura; for
anahata, supta vajrasana and matsyasana; for vishuddhi, sarvangasana;
and for ajna chakra, sirshasana and ashwa sanchalanasana. Halasana also
activates vishuddhi because the inflection is brought right up to the
upper cervical area. However, people who have a stiff upper cervical
spine should not do any of those upper spine flexion practices, because
the discs are very tiny at that part and these asanas can be too much.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Nischalananda]{.class5824-1} : Khandharasana is good for this
area. It's not so strong because a lot of the body weight is taken by
the feet.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Gaurishankar]{.class5824-1} : Let us get back to the subject of
depression.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : I think there are different
qualities in the thing that we call depression. The dread of the future
is one of the symptoms of depression and I think it is a mooladhara
chakra problem. But the dejection, lack of joy and loss of sense of
humour that you find in many people is due to a low energized
swadhisthana. With a low energized manipura comes loss of appetite and
low emotional activity.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[In depression there is a vicious circle; the whole mechanism, the whole
noradrenalin/dopamine mechanism]{.class-0} []{#part0064.xhtml_page_424
.class-0} [seems to slow down. It involves hormones. Most of the
anti-depressants act upon this noradrenalin/dopamine system.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : I would also imagine that
depletion of testosterone, excessive sexual activity, depletion of
adrenaline, excessive fear and anxiety, etc., all lead to a depressed
state.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : That is right. I have often
suspected too, that when the moon is new for instance, then people tend
to function to some extent on the energy of the lower chakras. The other
ones are functioning too, but it is the lower chakras that are carrying
a lot of the energy. Actually, the normal person experiences a depressed
feeling lasting a couple of days during that phase. Then the moon starts
activating the other chakras and the person comes out of it.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Nischalananda]{.class5824-1} : This relationship is also
indicated by the fact that some people go crazy at the time of full
moon. It means that energy comes up to and accumulates at ajna chakra.
The high energy affects the mind.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : It is strange that the medical
profession denies that the full moon has any effect on the mental state
of people, and there are comprehensive statistics from psychiatric
hospitals to show that the admission rate is no higher at the time of
the full moon than it is at the time of new moon. To this I say that
there are different conditions for which people are being admitted at
the time of the full moon and at the time of the new moon; this can be
seen most clearly.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : In hospitals, all the nursing
staff knows that when the full moon comes there are going to be
problems. There will be more road accidents, more crazy people coming in
and people going off their heads, etc.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Muktibodhananda]{.class5824-1} : What is the difference between
fear, anxiety and phobia?
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Fear is a normal response to a
threatening situation. If a tiger came into this room, nine people would
be frightened and that would be a natural response. Anxiety, on the
other hand, is really a collection []{#part0064.xhtml_page_425} of
symptoms which go on for a long time, usually not provoked by an
external situation. Phobias are immediate responses, just like fear,
except that the responses are to a non-threatening situation. A mouse a
hundred yards down the corridor, for instance, would not affect any of
us, but someone with a phobia about mice would panic.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : Phobias are actually a
displacement from an original object on to a different situation.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : That is the ego-defence mechanism
that Freud used to talk about. Freud used to talk about anxiety, psychic
complexes and so on, but the man in the taxi who had butterflies in the
stomach did have an accident which may have activated some old samskara
somewhere, which turned into a full fear of getting into his taxi. But
the whole thing was cleared so quickly; it was not deep-seated.
Sometimes I believe these things just build up in a susceptible moment
rather than in a susceptible person. They build up from a small bit of
anxiety to a bigger anxiety on the basis of a vicious circle. You break
that vicious circle anywhere and the whole thing just dissolves.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : The longer it is sustained the
more difficult it is to break.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : Each chakra has its own work to
perform and if one centre is blocked or diseased, then another centre
takes over its work. Because this work or function is being done by
another centre, it becomes perverted. This happens a lot if a person is
inhibited in swadhisthana chakra. Manipura will take over the work and
then the sexual activities will be just a power play, competition and
that sort of stuff -- completely perverted.
:::

::: {.class179 lang="en-us"}
[This perversion also occurs if manipura chakra takes over the job of
anahata. It is seen in do-gooders, those people who come and force you,
almost by threats of violence, to let them help you.]{.class-0}
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Shankardevananda]{.class5824-1} : Another example is of those
persons who get involved in a sexual encounter to fulfil the anahata
centre, and of course they don't get that fulfilment.
[]{#part0064.xhtml_page_426} This can lead to problems in marriage and
all the things you were saying about perversion of normal function.
:::

::: {.class52 lang="en-us"}
[Swami Vivekananda]{.class5824-1} : So the purpose of yoga is to balance
the functioning of the chakras and at the same time to awaken the
associated energies. Only then can we function as joyful, spontaneous
human beings, without depression, psychosis or physical problems. Only
when we balance and awaken all the chakras can life become meaningful.
:::

::: {.class1070 lang="en-us"}
:::

[\*](#part0064.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A6001) A discussion with the
swamis of Bihar School of Yoga, Munger, 1980
:::

| :::           | :::           | :::           | (ether)       | :::           | :::           | :::           | :::           |
|               |               |               | :::           |               |               |               |               |
+---------------+---------------+---------------+---------------+---------------+---------------+---------------+---------------+
| ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 | ::: class2455 |
| Ajna          | all five      | vijnanamaya   | manas (mind)  | clear or grey | mind          | mind          | mind          |
| :::           | :::           | :::           | :::           | circle        | :::           | :::           | :::           |
|               |               |               |               | :::           |               |               |               |

| :::           | :::           | :::           | :::           | :::           | :::           | :::           | :::           |

[]{#part0067.xhtml}

::: {#part0067.xhtml_page_433 .class4871 lang="en-us"}
[Glossary](#part0006.xhtml_k-4pqyFpS4aI3ekXWdsL9A5868)
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Adwaita]{.class5824-0} [-- non-dual; the concept of oneness.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Agni --]{.class5824-0} [fire.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Ajapa japa]{.class5824-0} [-- meditational practice in which mantra is
repeated in coordination with the ingoing and outgoing
breath.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Ajna chakra]{.class5824-0} [-- the psychic command centre situatedin
the midbrain.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Akasha]{.class5824-0} [-- ethereal space, e.g. the inner space before
the forehead known as chidakasha, the heart space known as hridayakasha,
and the ether of outer space known as mahakasha.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Amaroli]{.class5824-0} [-- yogic tantric practice in which the urine is
used either internally or externally for mental and physical
health.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Amrit]{.class5824-0} [-- psychic nectar which is secreted in bindu and
drops from lalana chakra to vishuddhi chakra, causing a feeling of
blissful intoxication.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Amygdala]{.class5824-0} [-- small area of grey matter in the temporal
lobe, part of the limbic system.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Anahata chakra]{.class5824-0} [-- the psychic centre related to the
region of the heart.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Anandamaya kosha]{.class5824-0} [-- blissful transcendental dimension;
personal and collective unconscious.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Annamaya kosha]{.class5824-0} [-- the physical body or level of
existence; the conscious aspect.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {#part0067.xhtml_page_434 .class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Aorta]{.class5824-0} [-- largest artery of the body, which takes
oxygenated blood from the heart for distribution throughout the
body.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Apana]{.class5824-0} [-- vital energy in the lower part of the body,
below the navel.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Asana]{.class5824-0} [-- a steady and comfortable position of the
body.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Ashram]{.class5824-0} [-- yogic community where the inmates live and
work under the guidance of a guru.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Astral body]{.class5824-0} [-- the subtle, psychic body; finer than the
physical body.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Atman]{.class5824-0} [-- the pure self, beyond body and
mind.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Atma shakti]{.class5824-0} [-- spiritual force.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Aushadhi]{.class5824-0} [-- awakening of spiritual power through the
use of herbs or plant preparations.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Autogenic training]{.class5824-0} [-- psychotherapy that works with the
body and mind simultaneously; learning to manipulate the bodily
functions through the mind.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Avatara]{.class5824-0} [-- divine incarnation.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Avidya]{.class5824-0} [-- ignorance.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Awareness]{.class5824-0} [-- the faculty of conscious
knowing.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Ballistocardiograph]{.class5824-0} [-- machine which measures small
body motions accompanying the movement of blood through the circulatory
system.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Bandha]{.class5824-0} [-- psychomuscular energy lock which redirects
the flow of psychic energy in the body.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Beeja mantra]{.class5824-0} [-- seed sound; a basic mantra or vibration
which has its origin in trance consciousness.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Bhajan]{.class5824-0} [-- devotional song.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Bhakta]{.class5824-0} [-- one who follows the path of bhakti
yoga.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Bhakti yoga]{.class5824-0} [-- the yoga of devotion.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Bhrumadhya]{.class5824-0} [-- the eyebrow centre; kshetram or contact
point for ajna chakra.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Bindu]{.class5824-0} [-- the psychic centre situated at the top back of
the head; a point or drop which is the substratum of the whole cosmos,
the seat of total creation.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Brahma]{.class5824-0} [-- the divine spirit, Hindu god; creator of the
universe.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {#part0067.xhtml_page_435 .class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Brahmacharya]{.class5824-0} [-- control and redirection of sexual
energy towards spiritual awakening.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Brahma granthi]{.class5824-0} [-- knot of creation. Psychomuscular knot
in the perineum which must be released for kundalini to enter and ascend
through sushumna nadi. It symbolizes the blockage posed by material and
sensual attachment.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Brahmamuhurta]{.class5824-0} [-- the time between 4 and 6 a.m. This is
the sattwic time of day, best suited to yogic sadhana.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Brahma nadi]{.class5824-0} [-- the most subtle pranic flow within the
sushumna nadi.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Brahmin]{.class5824-0} [-- a member of the priestly caste.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Buddhi]{.class5824-0} [-- the higher intelligence, concerned with real
wisdom; the faculty of valuing things for the advancement of life and
conscious awareness.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Causal body]{.class5824-0} [-- the body you experience in deep sleep
and in certain types of samadhi.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Central canal]{.class5824-0} [-- the hollow passage within the spinal
cord. In the subtle body, this is the path of sushumna nadi.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Cerebral cortex]{.class5824-0} [-- grey matter on the surface of the
brain responsible for higher mental function.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Cerebrospinal fluid]{.class5824-0} [-- (CSF) cushion of fluid
protecting the brain and spinal cord.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Cervical plexus]{.class5824-0} [-- autonomic nerve plexus in the neck
associated with vishuddhi chakra.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Cervix]{.class5824-0} [-- the circular opening leading into the womb;
seat of mooladhara chakra in the female body.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Chakra]{.class5824-0} [-- literally 'wheel' or 'vortex'; major psychic
centre in the subtle body, responsible for specific physiological and
psychic functions.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Chela]{.class5824-0} [-- disciple.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Chitta]{.class5824-0} [-- mind; conscious, subconscious and unconscious
levels of the brain.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Cingulate gyrus]{.class5824-0} [-- a convolution of the brain, part of
the limbic system.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Coccygeal plexus]{.class5824-0} [-- small nerve plexus at the base of
the spine behind the pelvic cavity, related to swadhisthana
chakra.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {#part0067.xhtml_page_436 .class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Consciousness]{.class5824-0} [-- the medium of universal and individual
awareness.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Corpus callosum]{.class5824-0} [-- fibres connecting the two
hemispheres of the brain.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Deity]{.class5824-0} [-- a form of divinity, a divine being having
subordinate functions.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Devata]{.class5824-0} [-- divine power.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Devi]{.class5824-0} [-- a goddess; a manifestation of
Shakti.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Dharana]{.class5824-0} [-- concentration; continuity of mental process
on one object or idea without leaving it.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Dharma]{.class5824-0} [-- duty; code of harmonious living; spiritual
path.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Dhumra lingam]{.class5824-0} [-- smoky (obscured) lingam; the symbol of
Shiva as manifest in mooladhara chakra.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Dhyana]{.class5824-0} [-- meditation, in the sense of intense
meditation for an extended period of time.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Diksha]{.class5824-0} [-- initiation into spiritual life by a
guru.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Dopamine]{.class5824-0} [-- chemical involved in the excitatory systems
of the brain.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Durga]{.class5824-0} [-- Hindu goddess; a personification of Shakti,
pictured riding upon a tiger, to whom personal ambition is
rendered.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Dwaita]{.class5824-0} [-- the philosophy of dualism in which man and
God are considered to be separated.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[ECG]{.class5824-0} [-- electrocardiogram. Tracing of electric current
produced by the heart.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[EEG]{.class5824-0} [-- electroencephalogram. Recording of electric
current produced by nerve cells in the brain.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[EMG]{.class5824-0} [-- electromyography. Recording of electrical
properties of muscles.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Epiglottis]{.class5824-0} [-- flap of cartilage at the back of the
throat which integrates the swallowing and breathing
processes.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Frontal lobe]{.class5824-0} [-- anterior portion of the brain
containing the motor area.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Ganga]{.class5824-0} [-- the river Ganges, the longest and most sacred
river in India.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Gauss]{.class5824-0} [-- measurement of intensity of a magnetic
field.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Granthis]{.class5824-0} [-- the three psychic knots on the sushumna
nadi]{.class-1} []{#part0067.xhtml_page_437 .class-1} [which hinder the
upward passage of kundalini -- brahma granthi, vishnu granthi and rudra
granthi.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Gunas]{.class5824-0} [-- the three qualities or matter of prakriti --
tamas, rajas and sattwa.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Guru]{.class5824-0} [-- literally, 'dispeller of darkness', the
spiritual master or teacher.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Guru chakra]{.class5824-0} [-- another name for ajna chakra, the eye of
intuition; through which the inner guru's guidance manifests.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Hatha yoga]{.class5824-0} [-- a system of yoga which specially deals
with practices for bodily purification.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Hippocampus]{.class5824-0} [-- an elevation on the floor of the lateral
ventricle, part of the limbic system.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Hiranyagarbha]{.class5824-0} [-- the golden egg; womb of consciousness,
the seat of supreme awareness in the crown of the head; known as
sahasrara chakra.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Hridayakasha]{.class5824-0} [-- the etheric space visualized within the
heart; the heart space.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Hypometabolic state]{.class5824-0} [-- state of lowered metabolism, for
example, decrease in respiratory, circulatory and secretory
rates.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Hypothalamus]{.class5824-0} [-- portion of the brain that integrates
temperature, sleep, food intake, development of sexual characteristics
and endocrine activity.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Ida]{.class5824-0} [-- major psychic channel which conducts manas
shakti, mental energy, located on the left side of the psychic body; the
'tha' of hatha yoga.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Indriyas]{.class5824-0} [-- sense organs.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Ishta devata]{.class5824-0} [-- one's personal symbol, form or vision
of God.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Itarakhya lingam]{.class5824-0} [-- symbol of Shiva in ajna
chakra.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Jalandhara bandha]{.class5824-0} [-- chin lock. It compresses the prana
in the trunk of the body and thereby helps to control psychic
energy.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Japa]{.class5824-0} [-- repetition of a mantra until it becomes the
spontaneous form of your conscious awareness.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Jivanmukta]{.class5824-0} [-- liberated soul, one who has attained
self-realization or moksha.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {#part0067.xhtml_page_438 .class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Jivatma]{.class5824-0} [-- the individual soul]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Jnana yoga]{.class5824-0} [-- path of yoga concerned directly with
knowledge, self-awareness.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Jnanendriyas]{.class5824-0} [-- the organs of knowledge or sensory
organs such eyes, ears, skin, etc.]{.class-1}
:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Jyotir lingam]{.class5824-0} [-- the symbol of Shiva in sahasrara
chakra. This lingam is of pure white light, symbolizing illumined astral
consciousness.]{.class-1}

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Vritti]{.class5824-0} [-- a modification arising in consciousness,

:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Vyana]{.class5824-0} [-- vital energy which pervades the whole

:::

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}
[Yoga]{.class5824-0} [-- union; the methods and practices leading to

::: {.class4873 lang="en-us"}

::: {.class5096 lang="en-us"}
[Yoga Sutras]{.class5824-0} [-- text written by Patanjali, delineating

[]{#part0070.xhtml}

:::::::::: {.class5298 lang="en-us"}
::::: class5290-0
:::: class5290-1
::: class5288
![](image5287.jpg){#page_454}
:::
::::
:::::

::: class5292
[Swami Satyananda]{.class6002} was born in Almora (Uttaranchal) in 1923.
Drawn to spiritual life from an early age, he left home at the age of
eighteen, and in 1943 surrendered himself to Swami Sivananda in
Rishikesh who initiated him into Dashnami sannyasa in 1947. He served
his guru for twelve years, perfecting every aspect of spiritual life.
Thereafter, he travelled throughout the Indian subcontinent as a
wandering ascetic.
:::

::: class5294
[Realizing the need of the times as scientific rendition of the ancient
system of yoga, he founded the International Yoga Fellowship in 1956 and
the Bihar School of Yoga in 1963. During the next twenty years, Swami
Satyananda hoisted the flag of yoga in every corner of the world,
consolidated BSY into a foremost institution of yoga, and authored over
eighty major texts on yoga, tantra and spiritual life.]{.class-8}
:::

::: class5294
['Satyananda Yoga' became a tradition which combines classical knowledge
with experiential understanding and a modern outlook. In 1984 he founded
the Yoga Research Foundation to synchronize scientific research and
yoga, and Sivananda Math to assist the underprivileged. In 1988, at the
peak of his achievements, he renounced everything and adopted kshetra
sannyasa, living as a paramahamsa ascetic. In 1989 Rikhia was revealed
to him, where he came to live and performed higher vedic sadhanas in
seclusion. Receiving the command to provide for his neighbours in 1991,
he allowed the ashram to help the underprivileged villages in the
region. From 1995 onwards, he performed a twelve-year Rajasooya Yajna
with the sankalpa of peace, plenty and prosperity for all, and in 2007
he announced the establishment of Rikhiapeeth with its mandate to
'serve, love, give'.]{.class-8}
:::

::: class5294
[Swami Satyananda attained mahasamadhi, a yogic accomplishment of
discarding the body at will to become one with the universal
consciousness, in 2009, in the presence of his disciples.]{.class-8}
:::
::::::::::
